فإن قلت : المسح كالتيمم بدلّ عن الغُسل، فيجب أن يشترط له النية كما شرطت لها. قلت : إنما شرطنا النيَّة في التيمم لدلالة الأدلة على ذلك، ولا دليل هاهنا ، ونظيره مسح الرأس؛ لكونهما مشتركين في كونهما طهارتين بالماء فكما لا يشترط في مسح الرأس شيء من ذلك لا يشترط فيه.
And what exceeds the measure of three fingers of the hand is only with used water. So he performed wudu and wiped over his khuffs, placing his right hand on his right khuff and his left hand on his left khuff, then he wiped their tops with one wipe, until it was as if I am looking at the fingers of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, on the khuffs. (1) Ibn Majah narrated from Jabir, may Allah be pleased with him: 'Indeed, the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, gestured with his hand like this from the tips of the fingers to the shin,' but its chain is weak. And al-Tabarani narrated in his al-Mu'jam al-Awsat from Jabir, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, passed by a man performing wudu while wiping his khuffs, so he nudged him with his hand and said: We were only commanded to wipe like this, and he extended his hand from the front of the khuffs to the shin once, and spread his fingers apart. (3) As mentioned by al-Ayni in al-Binayah. (4) 
[2] His saying: 'And what exceeds...': This statement has interpretations. First: The purpose is to clarify the consideration of three fingers and no more, and to rebut what is said: the established from the hadith is wiping with the fingers, and it is not restricted to three. The summary is that since it is known that wiping is with the fingers, if four or five fingers are considered, the excess wipe would be with used water, so it is not considered. Therefore, it does not enter into the obligatory. Its clarification: that what exceeds three is either with new water other than the water for the three, or with water used by the three. In the first case, it necessitates multiple wipes, and in the second, it necessitates the use of used water. But on this view: water of the hand, as long as it remains on the limb, does not take the ruling of used water until it separates from the limb, as has passed in its place. The better way in the estimation of three is that since it is established that the wiping of the Messenger of Allah was with the fingers, and the minimum of the plural is three, we said by presuming the certain amount without what exceeds it. 
(1) In Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah (1:170) and Sunan al-Bayhaqi al-Kabir (1:262), etc. (2) In Sunan Ibn Majah (1:183). (3) In al-Mu'jam al-Awsat (2:30-31). (4) Al-Binayah Sharh al-Hidayah (1:576), and see Nasb al-Rayah (1:180) and Khulasat al-Badr al-Munir (1:74), etc. 
Now the second interpretation: it is a rebuttal to what is said: it has passed that the Sunnah is wiping with spread fingers, so it necessitates increase over the amount of three due to the spreading of water from the three fingers into the spaces between them. Its summary is that what exceeds the three is only used water, not new water, so it is not considered, thus the amount of three remains. 
The third interpretation: it is a rebuttal to what is said: the Sunnah is to extend the fingers to the shin, so it necessitates increase over the amount of three. Its summary is that what exceeds its amount by extending is only with used water, so it is not considered. And in this context there are investigations of questions and answers, so seek them from al-Si'ayah. 
(1) His saying: 'So it is not considered': meaning it is not considered legally, so the amount of three fingers remains obligatory and the rest is void, or the meaning is it is not considered in necessitating increase over the prescribed amount. 
[2] His saying: 'anything else': i.e., other than the mentioned amount, such as intention, order, and continuity, due to lack of evidence indicating that. 
If you say: Wiping is like tayammum as a substitute for washing, so intention should be required for it as it was required for tayammum. I reply: We only required intention in tayammum due to the indication of evidences, and there is no evidence here. Its analogue is wiping over the head, because both are purifications with water. Just as nothing of that is required in wiping over the head, nothing is required in it.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of the amount of wiping over leather socks (khuffs). It begins by citing a hadith from Ibn Abi Shaybah and others describing how the Prophet (peace be upon him) wiped over his khuffs with three fingers. The author then discusses three interpretations (mahamil) of the phrase 'what exceeds three fingers.' The first interpretation holds that the obligatory amount is three fingers; any excess is with used water and thus not valid. The author notes that water on the limb is not considered used until it separates, but the preferred view is that the minimum plural (three) is taken as the certain amount. The second interpretation addresses the Sunnah of wiping with spread fingers, arguing that the water spreading into the gaps is still part of the used water, so only three fingers are counted. The third interpretation addresses extending fingers to the shin; again any excess beyond three fingers is with used water. The author then clarifies that 'no consideration' means the excess is not legally binding. He also explains that no additional conditions like intention (niyyah), order (tartib), or continuity (muwalat) are required for wiping over khuffs, analogous to wiping over the head, because those conditions are established only by clear evidence, which is lacking here. The passage concludes with a hypothetical objection comparing wiping to tayammum in requiring intention, and the response that tayammum requires intention due to specific evidence, while wiping over khuffs does not.

Key Terms
مسح (mash): Wiping over a body part or covering with wet hand without pouring water.
خف (khuff): A leather sock worn over the foot, which can be wiped over during wudu under certain conditions.
ماء مستعمل (ma' musta'mal): Water that has already been used for a ritual purification; Hanafis consider it no longer pure for purification.
ثلاث أصابع (thalath asabi'): Three fingers of the hand, which is the minimum obligatory amount for wiping over khuffs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Duration of Wiping Over Khuffs for a Resident
Ruling on time limit for wiping over khuffs for a resident

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the duration of wiping over khuffs for a resident and identify the opposing Maliki view.

Core Idea
The duration of wiping over khuffs is specified by time, not open-ended.

This passage opens the discussion on the time limit for wiping over khuffs (mash 'ala al-khuffayn). The Hanafi school, following the majority, holds that the duration is limited and distinguishes between a resident (24 hours) and a traveler (3 days). Imam Malik, however, considered it unlimited. The excerpt quotes from al-Nihayah and also includes an objection from Molla Khusro on a related point.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the passage and note the statement: 'The majority of scholars said: The duration of wiping is specified.' This is the Hanafi position.
2
Recognize the Dispute
The passage also mentions that Imam Malik said it is unspecified. Understand that this is a legitimate ikhtilaf between schools.
3
Understand the Practical Consequence
The difference matters: Hanafis have a time limit (24 hours for resident, 3 days for traveler), while Malikis allow wiping indefinitely as long as khuffs are not removed.
This consequence is called thamarah al-khilaf.
4
Set Context for Further Study
This passage only begins the discussion; the specific time limits and proofs will follow in later sections. For now, focus on the core dispute.
The passage is incomplete in this window.

Commentary
This passage begins the discussion on the duration of wiping over khuffs for a resident. It quotes from al-Nihayah that the majority of scholars (including the Hanafis) hold that the duration is limited (i.e., it has a time limit), while Imam Malik held it is unlimited (i.e., no time limit). The author notes that this ruling is not distinguished between resident and traveler in the source quoted. The passage then includes an objection from Molla Khusro to an earlier statement about extending fingers, but this objection is tangential. The main ruling here is that the Hanafi school follows the majority in limiting the duration, though the specific limit (e.g., 24 hours for a resident) is not mentioned in this excerpt. The passage is incomplete in this window; later sections will provide the exact duration and proofs.

Key Terms
مدة المسح (muddat al-mash): The specific time limit during which one may wipe over khuffs without removing them.
مقيم (muqim): A person who is not traveling; a resident who stays in one place.
مسافر (musafir): A traveler; someone who undertakes a journey of a certain distance (approx. 48 miles in Hanafi fiqh).

Obligatory Amount and Conditions for Wiping over Khuffs
Commentary explaining the fard amount and dismissing additional conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligatory amount of wiping over khuffs, explain why intention is not required, and apply the Hanafi ruling to a practical scenario.

Core Idea
Wiping three fingers is fard; intention, order, and continuity are not required.

This commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the exact obligatory amount for wiping over khuffs (masḥ ʿalā al-khuffayn) and refutes possible misunderstandings. The text emphasizes that the fard is limited to three fingers and that no other conditions—including intention, order, or continuity—are prescribed. We will dissect the reasoning behind this ruling, particularly the analogy to wiping the head and the distinction from tayammum.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fard amount
Locate the statement that the obligatory amount is three fingers. Note that any water beyond that is considered used water and therefore not effective.
The text uses 'فبقي مقدار ثلاث أصابع'.
2
Understand the two refuted objections
The author addresses two possible objections: (1) that the sunnah of spreading fingers would require more than three fingers, and (2) that the sunnah of extending to the shank would require more. His response shows the extra water is used water, so it is not considered.
These objections arise from misinterpreting sunnah acts as fard.
3
Recognize the absence of other conditions
The passage explicitly states that intention, order, and continuity are not prescribed because there is no evidence for them in this context.
Key phrase: 'ولا يفرض فيه شيء آخر كالنية وغيرها'.
4
Analyze the analogy and distinction
The commentator argues by qiyas: wiping over khuffs is like wiping the head (both are purifications with water), so just as intention etc. are not required for the head, they are not required for khuffs. He distinguishes from tayammum, which has its own textual proof for requiring intention.
This is a classic Hanafi usul argument.

So it is not considered, so the amount of three fingers remains, and nothing else is prescribed in it, like intention and others. Second: It is a rebuttal to what is said: It has passed that the sunnah is wiping with spread fingers, so it necessitates an increase beyond the amount of three due to the spread of water from the three fingers in their gaps. The summary is that what exceeds the three is only used water, not new water, so it is not considered, so the amount of three remains. Third: It is a rebuttal to what is said: The sunnah is extending the fingers to the shank, so it necessitates an increase beyond the amount of three. The summary is that what exceeds its amount by extension is only with used water, so it is not considered. And in this place there are discussions with questions and answers, so let them be sought from 'al-Sa'ayah'. (1) His saying: 'so it is not considered' means it is not considered legally, so the amount of three remains obligatory, and the rest is invalid; or the meaning is it is not considered in the necessity of increasing beyond the prescribed amount. [2] His saying: 'nothing else' i.e., other than the mentioned amount, like intention, order, and continuity, because there is no evidence indicating that. For you would say: Wiping is like tayammum as a substitute for washing, so intention should be required for it as it was required. I say: We only required intention in tayammum because proofs indicate that, but there is no proof here. And its analogy is wiping the head, because both are purifications with water; just as nothing of that is required in wiping the head, it is not required in it. (1) Mulla Khusraw objected in Durar al-Hikam (1:36) to the commentator's expression, saying: Because extending the fingers to the shank, if it is a sunnah, is not achieved except with purifying water, and they have agreed that used water is not purifying. Also they agreed that water as long as it is on the limb is not used water, so how can what was mentioned be correct?
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a commentary clarifying the obligatory amount of wiping over khuffs and the absence of other conditions. The author first states that the only fard amount is the area of three fingers; any water beyond that is considered used and therefore not effective. He then refutes two possible objections: (1) that according to the sunnah of wiping with spread fingers, more than three fingers would be required, but he argues that the extra water is used water; (2) that the sunnah of extending fingers to the shank would require more, but again the excess is used water. The author also explicitly states that no other requirements such as intention (niyyah), order (tartib), or continuity (muwalat) are prescribed, as there is no evidence for them. He addresses the objection that wiping over khuffs is like tayammum, which requires intention, by distinguishing that intention in tayammum is proven by specific evidence, and analogizing instead to wiping the head, which is a purification with water and does not require intention. Finally, he records an objection by Mulla Khusraw concerning used water when extending fingers, but refers readers to another work for the full discussion.

Key Terms
المسح (al-masḥ): The act of wiping over the khuffs with wet hands.
الثلاث أصابع (al-thalāth aṣābiʿ): The width of three fingers (of the hand) as the obligatory amount to wipe.
النية (al-niyyah): Intention – the author argues it is not required for wiping over khuffs.
الترتيب (al-tartīb): Order in performing the wiping – not required for masḥ.
الموالاة (al-muwālāh): Continuity (without interruption) – not required for wiping over khuffs.
الماء المستعمل (al-māʾ al-mustaʿmal): Used water – water that has already been used for purification and is no longer purifying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ḥanafī school, which of the following is NOT required for the validity of wiping over khuffs?
A) Wiping at least three fingers
B) Intention (niyyah)
C) Using pure water
D) Wiping on the top of the khuff

Key Takeaway
The obligatory part of wiping over khuffs is three fingers, and no conditions like intention, order, or continuity are required, based on the analogy with wiping the head and the lack of evidence otherwise.

The Time Limit for Wiping Over Khuffs
Explaining and defending the time limits for wiping over khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time limits for wiping over khuffs for a resident and a traveler, explain that the duration begins from the first hadath, and evaluate the Hanafi interpretation of the conflicting hadith.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is time-limited: one day for resident, three for traveler, starting from the first impurity after wearing.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on the duration of wiping over khuffs. The text specifies precise time limits and clarifies that the count begins not from wearing but from the first hadath. We also see how the Hanafi school handles a conflicting hadith from Malik's followers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act of wiping over khuffs. The ruling is that it is permissible but subject to a time limit: one day and night for a resident, three days and nights for a traveler.
This is a condition (shart) for the validity of wiping.
2
Understand the starting point
The duration begins from the first hadath (ritual impurity) that occurs after wearing the khuffs, not from the time of wearing. This is the position of the majority, including the Hanafi school.
For example, if one wears khuffs after wudu at Fajr and breaks wudu at Dhuhr, the count starts at Dhuhr.
3
Examine the dispute with Malik
Some scholars, including Imam Malik and al-Hasan al-Basri, hold that there is no time limit for a traveler. They rely on a hadith in which the Prophet said, 'If you are traveling, then wipe as you wish.'
This would allow a traveler to wipe indefinitely.
4
Interpret the hadith
The Hanafi response: The hadith does not cancel the time limit; rather it affirms that the ruling of wiping is ongoing (not abrogated). The time limit is established by other evidence (e.g., the hadith of `Ali and others).
Thus, the Hanafi position is that the limit remains: 3 days for a traveler.

Source Text

And perhaps you will notice from here that his saying in describing the traveler's duration: 'and their nights' – the idāfah (genitive construction) here is for minimal association, and the meaning is the nights that are taken with those days, whether they precede them or follow some of them. [2] His saying: 'and for the traveler' – an exception is made from it, and also from the context of the owner of the wound who is excused, for he is permitted to wipe as long as the time does not expire, not after it, even if this duration remains, as in Khulāṣat al-Fatāwā (2). [3] His saying: 'from the time of the hadath' – i.e., the beginning of this duration is considered from the time of the hadath, i.e., the first hadath that occurs after wearing. Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding the time limit for wiping over khuffs. The base text states: 'One day and night for the resident, and for the traveler three days and their nights, from the time of the hadath.' The commentator first notes that the majority of scholars hold the duration to be limited, while Imam Mālik and al-Ḥasan al-Baṣrī consider it unlimited, especially for the traveler. He then records a ḥadīth in which a man inquired about wiping up to seven days and the Prophet replied, 'If you are traveling, then wipe as you wish.' The Ḥanafī interpretation is that this ḥadīth affirms the perpetuity (taʾbīd) of the wiping concession, not that it removes the time limit set by other evidence. Next, the commentator explains the meaning of 'night' in the phrase: it includes both the preceding and following nights relative to the day. For example, if one wears the khuff at sunrise Friday, he may wipe until sunrise Saturday, even though the intervening night is not the night of Friday but of Saturday. Similarly, for the traveler, the 'nights' are those associated with the three days, whether preceding or following. He also notes an exception for a person with an excused condition (e.g., a wound) who may wipe for the entire period but must stop when the time exits. Finally, he clarifies that the duration count begins from the first ḥadath (ritual impurity) that occurs after putting on the khuffs, which is the position of the majority.

Key Terms
المقيم (al-muqīm): A person who is not traveling (resident) – for him the wiping duration is one day and night.
المسافر (al-musāfir): A traveler – for him the wiping duration is three days and nights.
من حين الحدث (min ḥīni al-ḥadath): From the time of the first ritual impurity (breaking wuḍūʾ) that occurs after putting on the khuffs.
الحدث (al-ḥadath): Ritual impurity that nullifies wuḍūʾ (like passing wind, urination, etc.).

Key Takeaway
The duration of wiping over khuffs is time-limited (1 day resident, 3 days traveler), starting from the first hadath after wearing, and the conflicting hadith is interpreted as affirming the concession, not canceling the limit.

Duration of Wiping over Khuff: From Hadath, Not from Wearing
Ruling on duration of mash with proof and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the duration of wiping over khuff for resident and traveler, identify the starting point (from the first hadath), and explain the Hanafi response to the opposing view of unlimited wiping.

Core Idea
The clock on wiping starts ticking from the first hadath, not from wearing the khuff — a crucial distinction for validity.

This passage clarifies the precise duration and beginning of the concession for wiping over leather socks. It also addresses a major inter-madhhab disagreement: can a traveler wipe indefinitely? The Hanafi school, relying on explicit hadiths, sets fixed limits, while others argue from a hadith that appears to grant unlimited permission. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to weigh scriptural evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the core ruling
Identify the duration: a resident may wipe for one day and one night; a traveler for three days and three nights.
The term 'night' includes both the preceding and following night, making the period continuous.
2
Determine the starting point
The duration begins from the first hadath (ritual impurity) after wearing the khuff, not from the moment of wearing or from the first wipe.
This is the majority view; alternative views from Ahmad and Hasan al-Basri are mentioned but not adopted.
3
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute
Malik and Hasan al-Basri hold that a traveler may wipe indefinitely, citing a hadith where the Prophet said 'wipe as long as you wish'. The Hanafi school interprets this as confirming the permissibility (rukhsah) is not abrogated, but the specific durations are fixed by other texts.
This shows how apparent general texts are restricted by more specific evidence in Hanafi usul.
4
Apply the ruling to an example
If one wears khuff at dawn, has a hadath after sunrise, then wipes at noon: the majority allow wiping until sunrise the next day. Work through the calculation.
Practice with different timing scenarios to internalize the principle.
5
Note exceptions and nullifiers
The perpetual excuse (sahib al-‘udhr) can wipe without time limit as long as the time for prayer remains. Whatever nullifies wudu also nullifies the wiping.
This ties the ruling to the broader topic of wudu nullifiers.

One day and one night, and for the traveler three days and their nights, from the time of the hadath. And Shaykh al-Islam said in his Mabsut: Malik said: The duration of wiping for the traveler is not limited, rather he may wipe as he wishes when he wears them with tahaarah. Imam al-Sarakhsi considered this the saying of al-Hasan al-Basri, who said: Wiping is perpetual for the traveler. And one who claimed perpetuity for the traveler argued with the hadith of a man who said: O Messenger of Allah, may I wipe for one day? He said: Yes. I said: Two days? He said: Yes, until I reached seven days, then he said: If you are on a journey, wipe as long as you wish. Its interpretation in our view is that the intent of the Prophet, peace be upon him, was to explain that wiping is not abrogated. (1) His saying: 'and a night' means with a night, and he did not say 'a night' to indicate that the night is more general than the preceding or following night. So if one wore the khuff at sunrise on Friday, for example, it is permissible for him to wipe until sunrise on Saturday, even though the night in this case is not the night of that day, for the night of a day according to the Shari'ah is the one preceding it. (2) His saying: 'for the traveler' excludes the one with a perpetual excuse, for it is permissible for him to wipe as long as the time has not passed, even if this period remains, as in Khulasat al-Fatawa. (3) His saying: 'from the time of the hadath' means the beginning of this period is considered from the time of the hadath: that is, the first hadath that occurs after wearing, and this is the saying of the majority. And in a narration from Ahmad: from the time one wipes after the hadath, and from al-Hasan al-Basri: from the time of wearing. So if one performs wudu at dawn, wears the khuff, and then has a hadath after sunrise, then performs wudu and wipes after noon, according to the saying of the majority it is permissible for him to wipe until sunrise of the second day, until dawn according to Ahmad, and until noon of the second day according to al-Hasan. (4) His saying: 'and that which nullifies wudu nullifies it' means everything that nullifies wudu; because wiping is a part of it, so if...
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on the duration of wiping over leather socks (khuff) and what nullifies it. The core ruling from the matn is that a resident wipes for one day and one night, and a traveler for three days and three nights, starting from the time of the first hadath after wearing the khuff. The commentary first addresses a historical disagreement: Imam Malik and Hasan al-Basri held that a traveler could wipe indefinitely as long as the khuff remains on, citing a hadith where the Prophet allowed wiping for as many days as needed. The Hanafi school interprets this hadith as confirming that the permission (rukhsah) is not abrogated, but it is limited by the explicit texts fixing the duration. Then the commentator clarifies the term 'night'—it includes both the night before and after the day, making it continuous. So if you wear the khuff at sunrise, your period includes the following night until the next sunrise. The phrase 'for the traveler' excludes the one with a chronic excuse (sahib al-‘udhr) who can wipe without time limit, as long as the time for prayer remains. The phrase 'from the time of the hadath' means the countdown begins when you have your first hadath after putting on the khuff, not from the moment of wearing. This is the majority view, but there are alternative narrations: Ahmad says from the time you first wipe after the hadath, and Hasan al-Basri says from the time of wearing. An example illustrates: if one performs wudu at dawn, wears the khuff, then has a hadath after sunrise, then performs wudu and wipes after noon, the majority allow wiping until sunrise the next day; Ahmad until dawn; Hasan until noon the next day. Finally, nullifiers: whatever nullifies wudu also nullifies the wiping, because wiping on the khuff is a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.

Key Terms
مسح على الخفين (mash 'ala al-khuffayn): Wiping over leather socks with wet hands as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.
مدة المسح (muddah al-mash): The time limit for wiping after the first hadath: one day+night for resident, three for traveler.
ناقض الوضوء (naqid al-wudu): Any event or action that nullifies wudu, such as using the toilet, passing wind, etc.; also nullifies the wiping over khuff.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) From the moment the khuff is worn.
B) From the first hadath after wearing.
C) From the first time the person wipes after wearing.
D) From the moment the person intends to wipe.

Key Takeaway
The duration for wiping over khuff is fixed from the first hadath after wearing, not from wearing itself, and the Hanafi school limits the traveler to three days contrary to the view of indefinite permission.

Removing One Khuff or Expiry of Mask Period
Ruling with proof on nullification of mask

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when one khuff is removed or the mask period expires, and explain the proof from the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Removing one khuff or expiry of the mask period nullifies wiping but wudu remains—only the feet need washing.

In Hanafi fiqh, wiping over khuffs is a temporary concession valid for a limited period. This lesson clarifies what happens when that concession is interrupted—either by removing a khuff or by the expiry of the prescribed time. The key point is that nullification of the mask does not nullify the entire wudu; only the feet need to be washed. This ruling is based on the action of a Companion and the legal principle that combining washing and wiping on the same limb in the same function is not permissible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its consequence
Determine what triggered the nullification: removing one khuff (naz') or expiry of the mask period (mudda). Recognize that both events have the same effect—the mask is invalidated.
The removal of even one khuff is sufficient to nullify the mask on both feet.
2
State the required action
After nullification, the person must wash both feet. The rest of the wudu remains intact; no need to repeat washing of face, hands, etc.
This is because the mask is a temporary substitute; once removed, the original obligation of washing revives.
3
Cite the proof
The author cites the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar: he removed his khuffs on an expedition, washed his feet, and did not repeat the entire wudu. This action demonstrates that removal nullifies the mask but not the wudu.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
4
Understand the legal reasoning
The khuff acts as a barrier preventing the spread of hadath (ritual impurity) to the foot. When removed, the barrier is gone, and the obligation to wash returns. Additionally, one cannot combine washing and wiping on the same limb in the same function, so if one foot must be washed, both must be washed.
This is a legal impossibility (ta'addhur shar'i), not a physical one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونزع الخف) ، ذكر لفظ الواحد ، ولم يقل : نزع الخفين ؛ ليفيد أن نزع أحدهما ناقض ، فإنه إذا نزع أحدهما وجب غسل إحدى الرجلين"، فوجب غسل الأخرى، إذ لا جمع بين الغسل والمسح ، وكذا إن دخل الماء أحد خفيه حتى صار جميع الرجل مغسولاً انتقض فيجب تجديد المسح عند تجديد الوضوء عند بقاء المدة. [١] قوله : ونزع الخف ؛ لما روي عن عبد الله بن عمر له «أنه كان في غزوة فنزع خفيه وغسل قدميه ولم يعد الوضوء» (١) ، وهكذا روي عن غيره من أصحاب رسول الله فعلم أن الحدث إنما يزول بالمسح مؤقتاً لا مؤبداً. كذا في «حواشي الهداية» لملا الهداد (٢) الجونفوري. [٢]قوله : وجب غسل إحدى الرجلين ؛ وهو الذي نزعه منه ؛ لسراية الحدث إلى القدم، حيث زال الخف المانع ، فإن الخف عهد شرعاً مانعاً عن سراية الحدث إلى ما فيه. [٣]قوله : فوجب ؛ قال صاحب «الهداية»: «وكذا نزع أحدهما ؛ لتعذر الجمع بين الغسل والمسح في وظيفة واحدة». انتهى قال الجونفوري في «حواشيه»: «يعني المسح مع الغسل لم يشرع ؛ إذ المسح طهارة غير معقولة، فيقتصر على مورد الشرع، فالمراد بالتعذر التعذر الشرعي، أو المراد أنه يتعذر حكم الجمع بينهما. قوله : إذ لا جمع ؛ يعني لا جمع في الشرع بين الغسل والمسح : أي في وظيفة واحدة، وأما عند تعدّد الوظيفة فالجمع موجود ؛ كغسل الوجه واليدين والرجلين مع مسح الرأس في الوضوء، فلو مسح على الخف الواحدة، وغسل إحدى الرجلين لزم الجمع بينهما في وظيفة واحدة متعلقة بالرجلين. [0]قوله : جميع الرجل مغسولاً ؛ قال قاضي خان في «فتاواه»: «ماسح الخف إذا دخل الماء في خفه وابتل من رجله قدر ثلاثة أصابع أو أقل لا يبطل مسحه؛ لأن هذا القدر لا يجزئ عن غسل الرجل، فلا يبطل به حكم المسح، وإن ابتل جميع القدم وبلغ الماء الكعب بطل المسح يروى ذلك عن أبي حنيفة». انتهى ثم قال: "ومضي المدة، وبعد أحد هذين على المتوضئ غسل رجليه فحسب : أي على الذي كان له وضوء لا يجب إلا غسل رجليه، أي لا يجب غسل بقية الأعضاء"
And the removal of the khuff) He mentioned the singular word, and did not say: removal of the two khuffs; to indicate that removal of one of them is a nullifier. Because if he removes one of them, washing one foot becomes obligatory, then washing the other becomes obligatory, since there is no combining washing and wiping. Similarly, if water enters one of his khuffs until the entire foot becomes washed, it is nullified, so it becomes obligatory to renew the wiping when renewing the wudu while the period remains. [1] His statement: And removal of the khuff; based on what was narrated from Abdullah ibn Umar that he was on an expedition, so he removed his two khuffs and washed his feet and did not repeat the wudu. Similarly, it was narrated from other companions of the Messenger of Allah, so it is known that the ritual impurity is only removed by wiping temporarily, not permanently. Likewise in Hawashi al-Hidayah by Mulla al-Hidad al-Jawnpuri. [2] His statement: Washing one foot became obligatory; i.e., the foot from which he removed it; because of the spread of the ritual impurity to the foot, since the khuff—which was a barrier—was removed. For the khuff is considered in Shari'ah as a barrier preventing the spread of ritual impurity to what is inside it. [3] His statement: So it became obligatory; said the author of al-Hidayah: 'And similarly, removing one of them; because it is impossible to combine washing and wiping in one function.' End. Al-Jawnpuri said in his Hawashi: 'He means that wiping with washing is not legislated; because wiping is an unintelligible purification, so it is confined to where it is prescribed by Shari'ah. The meaning of impossibility is legal impossibility, or it means that the ruling of combining them is impossible.' His statement: Since there is no combining; he means there is no combining in Shari'ah between washing and wiping: i.e., in one function. As for when the functions are multiple, combining exists; like washing the face and hands and feet with wiping the head in wudu. If he were to wipe over one khuff and wash one foot, combining would be necessary in one function related to the feet. [0] His statement: The entire foot becomes washed; Qadikhan said in his Fatawa: 'If water enters the khuff of one who is wiping and wets his foot to the extent of three fingers or less, his wiping is not invalidated; because this amount does not suffice for washing the foot, so the ruling of wiping is not invalidated. If the entire foot becomes wet and the water reaches the ankle, the wiping is invalidated. That is narrated from Abu Hanifah.' End. Then he said: "And the expiry of the period, and after either of these two, what is obligatory upon the one who has wudu is only washing his feet: i.e., upon the one who had wudu, it is not obligatory except washing his feet, i.e., washing the rest of the limbs is not obligatory."
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling regarding removal of the khuff and expiry of the wiping period. The author clarifies that removing one khuff, not just both, nullifies the wiping. The proof is the action of Abdullah ibn Umar, who removed his khuffs and washed his feet without repeating the entire wudu. The reasoning is that the khuff is a barrier; once removed, the underlying foot is subject to the obligation of washing. Since one cannot combine washing and wiping on the same limb in one function, if one foot is washed, the other must also be washed because they are one legal unit. Similarly, if water enters the khuff and wets the entire foot, the wiping is nullified and the foot must be washed. If only part of the foot is wet (less than three fingers), the wiping remains valid because that amount does not constitute washing. The passage also discusses the expiry of the period: when the prescribed time for wiping ends, the person must only wash his feet—not repeat the entire wudu—because the previous wudu is still valid for the other parts. This is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Key Terms
نزع (naz'): Removal of the khuff from the foot.
مدة (mudda): The prescribed period for wiping over khuffs (one day and one night for resident, three days and nights for traveller).
مسح (mask): Wiping over khuffs as a substitute for washing feet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person removes one khuff during his mask period, what must he do?
A) Wash both feet and renew the entire wudu
B) Wash only the foot whose khuff was removed, then continue
C) Wash both feet, and his wudu remains valid for other parts
D) Nothing, he can put the khuff back on and continue wiping

Key Takeaway
Removing one khuff or expiry of the mask period nullifies wiping over khuffs; only the feet need washing, and the wudu remains valid for the other parts.

Water Entering the Khuff: When Does It Invalidate the Mask?
Ruling on water entering khuff and mask validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on water entering the khuff and identify when it invalidates the mask, distinguishing between complete and partial wetting.

Core Idea
Only complete wetting of the foot invalidates the mask over khuffs; partial wetting does not.

This passage expands on a specific scenario within the rules of wiping over khuffs: what happens when water enters the khuff and reaches the foot? The Hanafi school has a clear threshold – only if the entire foot becomes wet is the mask invalidated. A minority view within the school considers a majority sufficient, but the relied-upon position is that complete wetting is required. The passage also touches on the expiry of the mask period and a fatwa regarding extreme cold, where Ibn al-Humam's response reinforces the priority of tayammum over continued wiping.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule under discussion
Determine what act is being ruled upon: water entering the khuff and its effect on the validity of the mask (wiping).
2
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
According to Abu Hanifa, if water wets the entire foot up to the ankle, the mask is invalidated and washing becomes obligatory. If only part is wet, mask remains valid.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Ja'far al-Hindawi argued that if a majority of the foot is wet, it has the same ruling as the whole. The text prefers the view that only complete wetting invalidates.
4
Examine the expiry of the mask period
When the mask period expires, wiping is no longer allowed even if not performed. Nullification is attributed to expiry or removal, but the true nullifier is the original hadath (impurity).
5
Evaluate the cold fear exception
Some fatwas allow a traveler to continue wiping if period expired and removing khuff would cause severe cold harm. Ibn al-Humam rejects this, requiring tayammum instead of continued wiping.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن أصاب الماء أكثرها ، فكذا عند الفقيه أبي جعفر الهنداوي بناء على أن للأكثر حكم الكل، فيجب عليه أن ينزع الخف ويغسل كل القدم ، وقيل : لا يعتبر ذلك إلا أن يصير جميع القدم مغسولاً. قوله : ومضي المدة ؛ أي المدة المذكورة وإن لم يمسح فيها بأن لبس الخف ثم أحدث بعده ثم مضت المدة بعد الحدث ولم يمسح فيها، ليس له المسح، ونسبة النقض إلى مضي المدة، وكذا إلى نزع الخف باعتبار ظهور النقض عندهما، وإلا فالناقض في الحقيقة في هاتين الصورتين هو الحدث السابق. وذكر في فتاوى قاضي خان» و «مختارات النوازل» و «الخلاصة» و«التاتارخانية» و«الولوالجية» وغيرها : أنه إذا انقضت مدة المسح وهو مسافر ويخاف ذهاب رجله من البرد لو نزع خفيه جاز له المسح. وفيه ما ذكره ابن الهمام في «فتح القدير»: «إن خوف البرد لا أثر له في منع السراية، كما أنّ عدم الماء لا يمنعها، فغاية الأمر أنه لا ينزع ، لكن لا يمسح، بل يتيمم لخوف البرد».
And if water touches most of it, then similarly according to al-Faqih Abu Ja'far al-Hindawi, based on the principle that the majority has the ruling of the whole, so it becomes obligatory for him to remove the khuff and wash the entire foot. And it is said that it is not considered unless the entire foot becomes washed. His statement: And the expiry of the period; i.e., the mentioned period, even if he did not wipe within it—such that he put on the khuff, then became impure afterwards, then the period expired after the impurity and he did not wipe within it—he does not have the option to wipe. The attribution of nullification to the expiry of the period, and likewise to the removal of the khuff, is based on the appearance of nullification according to them; otherwise, the actual nullifier in these two cases is the prior impurity. And it is mentioned in Fatawa Qadikhan, Mukhtarat al-Nawazil, al-Khulasah, al-Tatarkhaniyyah, al-Walwaljiyyah, and others: that if the period of wiping has expired while he is a traveller and he fears the loss of his foot from cold if he removes his khuffs, it is permissible for him to continue wiping. Regarding this, Ibn al-Humam mentioned in Fath al-Qadir: 'Indeed, fear of cold has no effect in preventing the spread [of impurity], just as lack of water does not prevent it. The upshot is that he does not remove [the khuff], but he does not wipe; rather, he performs tayammum due to fear of cold.'
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage discusses the scenario where water enters the khuff and wets the foot. According to Abu Hanifa, if water covers the entire foot up to the ankle, the wiping is invalidated—even if the water came from outside—because the foot has effectively become wet, making washing rather than wiping applicable. If only part of the foot is wet (less than three fingers), the wiping remains valid. There is a difference of opinion: Abu Ja'far al-Hindawi holds that if the majority of the foot is wet, it has the same ruling as the whole, so removal and full washing are required. The preferred view, however, is that only complete wetting invalidates. The passage then returns to the issue of period expiry. When the mask period ends, the person may not continue wiping, even if he has not wiped during that time. The nullification is attributed to expiry or removal, though the true nullifier is the original ritual impurity (hadath) that occurred before. Finally, a fatwa from several works permits a traveller, whose period has expired, to continue wiping if he fears severe cold damage—but Ibn al-Humam rejects this, saying tayammum is the proper substitute, not continued wiping, because fear does not prevent the spread of impurity.

Key Terms
دخل الماء (dakhala al-ma'): Water entering the khuff and reaching the foot.
أكثرها (aktharuha): Majority of the foot being wet.
خوف البرد (khawf al-bard): Fear of cold causing harm to the foot if khuff is removed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is wiping over khuffs and water enters his khuff, wetting only the toes (less than three fingers), what is the ruling?
A) The mask is invalidated and he must wash his foot
B) The mask remains valid because the wetting is insufficient for washing
C) He must remove the khuff and perform tayammum
D) He can continue wiping as if nothing happened

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, only complete wetting of the foot (up to ankle) invalidates the mask over khuffs; partial wetting does not, and a fatwa allowing continued wiping due to cold is overruled by Ibn al-Humam's opinion requiring tayammum.

Threshold for Invalidation of Wiping Due to Water Entering the Khuff
Commentary on the ruling when water enters the khuff and wets the foot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when water entering the khuff invalidates wiping, distinguish between the two intra-Hanafi opinions, and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is invalidated only when the foot becomes entirely wet (or majority), not by a small amount like three fingers.

Imagine you are performing wudu and water accidentally seeps into your leather sock (khuff). Does a splash nullify your wiping? The Hanafi school provides a precise threshold based on how much of the foot becomes wet. This lesson unpacks the text from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, where the commentator clarifies the ruling and presents an internal disagreement among Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key scenario
The passage describes a person who already has wudu and is wiping over khuffs. Water enters the khuff and wets part of the foot. Determine whether this invalidates the wiping (mas-h).
2
Apply the quantitative threshold
The text states a clear rule: if the wet area is three fingers or less, wiping remains valid. If the entire foot up to the ankles becomes wet, wiping is invalidated. Memorize this threshold.
Three fingers is the minimal amount that would suffice for washing in a full wudu, but here it is insufficient to replace wiping.
3
Analyze the intermediate case
What if most of the foot is wet but not all? The commentator presents two views: al-Hindawi considers the majority equivalent to the whole, requiring removal of the khuff and full washing; another view restricts invalidation to complete wetting.
The first view is given weight (mufta bihi) in this text.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The difference stems from the legal maxim that 'the majority has the ruling of the whole' (al-akthar yanazil manzilat al-kull). Recognize how this maxim is applied in different schools.
5
Connect to the overall nullification of wiping
The passage also reminds that the actual nullifier of the concession of wiping is the original hadath (impurity), while removal of the khuff or expiry of the period are merely signs of nullification.
Water entering the khuff does not nullify the wiping by itself; it only does so if it effectively washes the foot, thus rendering the wiping superfluous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة / المسح على الخفين
ومضي المدة، وبعد أحد هذين على المتوضئ غَسْلُ رجليه فحسب
وإن أصابَ الماءُ أكثرها ، فكذا عند الفقيه أبي الجعفر [؟] ( ومضي المدة"، وبعد أحد هذين : أي نَزَعُ الخُفَّ، ومُضِي المدَّة، (على المتوضئ غسل رجليه فحسب : أي على الذي كان له وضوء لا يَجِبُ إِلا غَسْلُ رجليه ، أي لا يَجِبُ غَسْلُ بقية الأعضاء
(1)
دخل الماء في خُفّه وابتل من رجلِهِ قدر ثلاثة أصابع أو أقل لا يبطل مسحه ؛ لأنَّ هذا القدر لا يجزئ عن غسل الرجل ، فلا يبطل به حكم المسح ، وإن ابتل جميع القدم وبلغ الماء الكعب بَطَلَ المسح يروى ذلك عن أبي حنيفة ». انتهى [1] قوله : فكذا عند الفقيه أبي جعفر ؛ الهنداوي بناءً على أن للأكثر حكم الكل، فيجب عليه أن ينزع الخف ويغسل كلَّ القدم ، وقيل : لا يعتبر ذلك إلا أن يصير جميعُ القدم مغسولاً. (۲) قوله : ومضي المدة ؛ أي المدة المذكورة وإن لم يمسح فيها بأن لبس الخُفَّ ثم أحدث بعده ثم مضت المدَّةُ بعد الحدث ولم يمسح فيها، ليس له المسح، ونسبة النقض إلى مضي المدة، وكذا إلى نزع الخف باعتبارِ ظهورِ النقض عندهما، وإلا فالنَّاقض في الحقيقة في هاتين الصورتين هو الحدث السابق.
Book of Purification / Wiping over Khuffs. And the period passes, and after one of these two, the one who has wudu must only wash his feet. If water hits most of it, then also according to al-Faqih Abi Ja'far [؟] (And the period passes). After one of these two: meaning removal of the khuff and passing of the period. (For the one who has wudu, he must only wash his feet: meaning one who had wudu, only washing his feet is obligatory, i.e., washing the rest of the limbs is not obligatory. (1) Water enters his khuff and wets his foot to the extent of three fingers or less: it does not invalidate his wiping; because this amount does not suffice for washing the foot, so the ruling of wiping is not invalidated. If the entire foot becomes wet and the water reaches the ankles, the wiping is invalidated. This is narrated from Abu Hanifa. End [1] His statement: Similarly according to al-Faqih Abi Ja'far al-Hindawi, based on the principle that the majority has the ruling of the whole; so he must remove the khuff and wash the entire foot. And it is said: this is not considered unless the entire foot becomes washed. (2) His statement: And the period passes; meaning the mentioned period, even if he did not wipe during it; that is, he wore the khuff, then had an event, and then the period passed after the event and he did not wipe; he may not wipe. The nullification is attributed to the passing of the period, and similarly to the removal of the khuff, by way of the appearance of nullification with them; otherwise, the actual nullifier in these two cases is the prior event.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This is an expansion probe from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah. The passage addresses two scenarios after the khuff is removed or the wiping period expires: the person with prior wudu only needs to wash his feet, not the rest of the limbs. Then it discusses the effect of water entering the khuff. If less than three fingers of the foot become wet, wiping is not invalidated because that amount does not replace the full washing. If the entire foot up to the ankles becomes wet, wiping is invalidated. There is a disagreement about when most of the foot becomes wet: according to al-Faqih Abi Ja'far al-Hindawi, the majority takes the ruling of the whole, so he must remove the khuff and wash the entire foot; another opinion says it is only considered if the whole foot is washed. The commentator then clarifies that the passing of the period, even without having wiped, prevents further wiping, but the true cause of nullification is the original hadath.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): Leather sock worn over the foot, over which wiping is permitted in wudu.
المسح (al-mas-h): The act of wiping over the khuff instead of washing the feet.
النقض (al-naqd): Nullification of the wiping due to removal of khuff or passing of period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The wiping is invalidated because the foot became wet.
B) The wiping remains valid because less than three fingers are wet.
C) The wiping is invalidated only if the water reaches the ankle.
D) The wiping becomes invalid and must be repeated.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs remains valid unless the foot becomes entirely wet (or the majority according to one view), because a small amount of water does not suffice for washing.

intermediate
6 min
Ruling when wiping period expires while fearing cold
Dispute among Hanafi authorities on wiping vs. tayammum after period expires with fear of cold

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a traveler's wiping period expires and he fears cold damage, and explain the disagreement between Ibn al-Humam and the majority.

Core Idea
Fear of cold does not extend the wiping period, but the dominant Hanafi view allows continued wiping based on transmitted texts.

When a traveler's wiping period for khuffs expires, the normal rule is that he must remove them and wash his feet. However, an exceptional case arises when he fears his feet will be harmed by cold upon removal. This lesson examines a scholarly disagreement within the Hanafi school: should he perform tayammum or may he continue to wipe? The dispute centers on whether fear of cold prevents the legal effect of the period's expiry.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
Identify the ruling upheld by most Hanafi authorities: that the traveler may continue to wipe despite the expiry of the period, due to the excuse of fear of cold.
This view is transmitted from al-Kafi, Uyun al-Madhahib, al-Jawami', and others.
2
Identify the opposing view
Recognize that Ibn al-Humam (and a few others) object, arguing that fear of cold does not stop the period from running its course, so wiping becomes invalid and tayammum must be performed.
Ibn al-Humam's view is based on the principle that the period (sarayah) is not affected by excuses.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand Ibn al-Humam's reasoning: just as lack of water does not prevent the end of the period, fear of cold does not either. Therefore, the only excuse to avoid removing is tayammum, not wiping.
He analogizes with the case of inability to use water.
4
Analyze the majority response
The majority relies on transmitted rulings from earlier authorities that explicitly allow wiping in this case. They argue that fear of cold is a valid excuse that justifies continuing to wipe, and Ibn al-Humam's reasoning contradicts established practice.
Later scholars like al-Allamah Qasim dismiss Ibn al-Humam's research as contrary to the transmitted (manqul).
5
Determine the practical difference
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: if one follows the majority, he may wipe and pray; if he follows Ibn al-Humam, he must perform tayammum and pray without wiping.
The dominant practice is to follow the majority view.

Source Text

(۲) انتهى من «فتح القدير (١) : (١٥٤) بتصرف. قال ابن عابدين في رد المحتار» (١ : ٢٤٦) : فالحاصل أن المسألة مصورة فيما إذا مضت مدة المسح وهو متوضئ وخاف إن نزع الخف لغسل رجليه من البرد وإلا أشكل تصوير المسألة ؛ لأنه إذا خاف على رجليه يلزم منه الخوف على بقية الأعضاء فإنها ألطف من الرجلين ، وإذا خاف ذلك يكون عاجزاً عن استعمال الماء

فيلزمه العدول إلى التيمم بدلاً عن الوضوء بتمامه، ولا يحتاج إلى مسح الخف أصلاً مع التيمم حيث تحققت الضرورة المبيحة له.....
والذي حققه في «البدائع» بحثا لزوم التيمم دون المسح ، فإنه بعـد مـا نقـل عـن جوامع الفقه» و«المحيط» أنه إن خاف البرد فله أن يمسح مطلقاً أي بلا توقيت . قال ما نصه : فيه نظر ، فإن خوف البرد لا أثر له في منع السراية ، كما أن . عدم الماء لا يمنعها، فغاية الأمر أنه لا ينزع ، لكن لا يمسح بل يتيمم لخوف البرد . اهـ وأقره في شرح المنية وأطنب في حسنه ؛ وهو صريح في انتقاض المسح لسراية الحدث، فلا يصلي به إلا بعد التيمم لا المسح. ولكن المنقول هو المسح لا التيمم كما مر عن الكافي» و «عيون المذاهب» و«الجوامع» ، وبه صرح الزيلعي وقاضي خان والقهستاني عن «الخلاصة»، وكذا في «التاتارخانية» و«الولوالجية» و«السراج» عن «المشكل» ، وكذا في «مختارات النوازل» لصاحب
و«المحيط»
الهداية
، وبه صرح أيضاً في «المعراج» و «الحاوي القدسي» بزيادة جعله كالجبيرة، وعليه مشى في «الإمداد». وقد قال العلامة قاسم : لا عبرة بأبحاث شيخنا يعني ابن الهمام إذا خالفت
المنقول. فافهم». (۱) «الهداية» (۱ : ۲۹) ، وكذلك صاحب الدر المختار» (۱) : (١٨٤) خروج أكثر القدم، وهو المروي عن أبي يوسف الله له ، وبه جزم في «الكنز» (ص (٦) ، و«الملتقى»(ص)، وهو لأن فيه
And it is mentioned in Fatawa Qadikhan, Mukhtarat al-Nawazil, al-Khulasah, al-Tatarkhaniyyah, al-Walwalijiyyah and others: that if the period of wiping expires while he is a traveler and he fears his foot will be lost due to cold if he removes his khuffs, he may wipe. There is in it what Ibn al-Humam mentioned in Fath al-Qadir: 'Fear of cold has no effect in preventing the period from ending, just as lack of water does not prevent it. The extent of the matter is that he does not remove, but he does not wipe; rather, he performs tayammum due to fear of cold.' (2) (1) From Fatawa Qadikhan (1:50). (2) Ended from Fath al-Qadir (1:154) with modification. Ibn Abidin said in Radd al-Muhtar (1:246): So the conclusion is that the issue is pictured when the period of wiping passes while he has wudu and fears if he removes the khuff to wash his feet from the cold; otherwise the depiction of the issue is problematic; because if he fears for his feet, it follows that he fears for the rest of the limbs, as they are more delicate than the feet, and if he fears that, he becomes unable to use water. So he must turn to tayammum instead of complete wudu, and he does not need to wipe the khuff at all with tayammum when the necessity that permits it is realized. And what he verified in al-Bada'i' is a research on the necessity of tayammum without wiping, for after he transmitted from Jawaami' al-Fiqh and al-Muhit that if he fears cold, he may wipe absolutely, i.e., without time limit. He said its text: 'There is consideration in it, for fear of cold has no effect in preventing the period from ending, just as lack of water does not prevent it. The extent of the matter is that he does not remove, but he does not wipe; rather, he performs tayammum due to fear of cold.' End. And he approved it in Sharh al-Munyah and elaborated on its goodness; and it is explicit that the wiping is invalidated by the passing of hadath, so he cannot pray with it except after tayammum, not wiping. But what is transmitted is wiping, not tayammum, as mentioned from al-Kafi, Uyun al-Madhahib, al-Jawami', and it is stated by al-Zaylai, Qadikhan, and al-Qahistani from al-Khulasah, and similarly in al-Tatarkhaniyyah, al-Walwalijiyyah, and al-Siraj from al-Mushkil, and similarly in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil of the author of al-Muhit, al-Hidayah, and it is also stated in al-Mi'raj and al-Hawi al-Qudsi with the addition of making it like a splint (jabirah), and upon it he proceeded in al-Imdad. And al-Allamah Qasim said: 'No consideration is given to the researches of our shaykh meaning Ibn al-Humam when they contradict what is transmitted. So understand.' (1) Al-Hidayah (1:29), and similarly the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar (1:184): 'emergence of most of the foot' – which is narrated from Abu Yusuf, and he declared it in al-Kanz (p. 6) and al-Multaqa (p.), and it is because in it
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute within the Hanafi school, presented as a critical refinement. The issue is whether a traveler whose wiping period has expired may continue to wipe if he fears his feet will be harmed by cold upon removing the khuffs. Many authorities (Qadikhan, etc.) allow wiping. However, Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir argues that fear of cold does not prevent the invalidation of the wiping by the passing of time; so he should not wipe but instead perform tayammum due to the excuse. Ibn Abidin clarifies that the scenario is when the period expires while he still has wudu and fears cold on removing, otherwise if he feared for his feet, he would also fear for other limbs, making him unable to use water entirely. There is a strong transmitted opinion (al-Kafi, etc.) allowing wiping, and later scholars like al-Allamah Qasim dismiss Ibn al-Humam's research as contrary to the transmitted view. The passage concludes with a note from al-Hidayah favoring the position that most of the foot emerging is like removal, but the main dispute here is about the period expiry with fear of cold.

Key Terms
السراية (al-sarayah): The passage of the period of wiping; here meaning that the period continues to run regardless of fear of cold.
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution with dust as a substitute for wudu when water is unavailable or harmful.
الجبيرة (al-jabirah): A splint; in fiqh, wiping over a splint is allowed. Here, some analogize the khuff to a splint in case of necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the transmitted opinion from al-Kafi and others, what should a traveler do if the wiping period expires and he fears his feet will freeze?
A) He must remove the khuffs and wash his feet in cold water.
B) He may continue wiping despite the expiry of the period.
C) He must perform tayammum instead of wiping.
D) He should delay prayer until the cold subsides.

Key Takeaway
When a traveler's wiping period expires and he fears cold damage, the dominant Hanafi position allows continued wiping based on transmitted texts, rejecting Ibn al-Humam's insistence on tayammum.

Invalidation of Wiping by Exposure of the Foot from the Khuff
Ruling on emergence of heel/foot from khuff.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when most of the heel or foot emerges from the khuff and identify the conditions that invalidate or preserve the validity of wiping.

Core Idea
Emergence of most of the foot from the khuff with intent to remove invalidates wiping; a temporarily lifted heel in a wide khuff does not.

This passage from `Umdat al-Ri`ayah clarifies a specific ruling about wiping over khuffs. It addresses what constitutes removal (naz`) when most of the heel or foot emerges, and distinguishes between intentional exposure and incidental movement in a loose khuff. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the concession of wiping over khuffs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over the khuff. The ruling here concerns when that wiping becomes invalidated due to exposure of the foot.
The base ruling is that wiping is permissible.
2
Understand the nullifier
The nullifier is the emergence of most of the foot (or heel) from the khuff, but only if done with the intention to remove the khuff.
Intention is a key condition.
3
Distinguish the exception
If the khuff is wide and the heel lifts out temporarily but returns to its place, wiping is not invalidated, even if most of the heel was exposed momentarily.
This is based on the text from al-Muhit.
4
Note the preferred textual wording
Al-Quduri uses 'most of the foot', while others use 'most of the heel'. Al-Hidayah confirms 'most of the foot' as the correct (sahih) criterion.
The mufta bihi position is 'most of the foot'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخروج أكثر العقب إلى الساق نَزْع، ولفظ القُدُوري : أكثر القدم
[١]قوله : وينبغي ؛ أشار به إلى أنه لم يجد تصريحاً في ذلك، لكن قواعده تقتضيه. [٢] قوله : وخروج أكثر العقب ؛ - بفتح العين المهملة، وسكون القاف، وجاء كسر العين أيضاً مع سكون القاف وفتح العين مع كسر القاف - : مؤخّر القدم إلى موضع الشراك. كذا في مجمع البحار».
وفي إيراده مفرداً إشارة إلى أن خروج الأكثر من أحدهما أيضاً ناقض، وهذا إذا كان بنية نزع الخف، أما إذا لم يكن بنيته فلا يبطل المسحُ إجماعاً، كذا في «النهاية»، وفي «المحيط»: «إذا كان الخف واسعاً بحيث إذا رفع القدم ارتفع العقب، وإذا رجع عاد إلى موضعه، فلا بأس بالمسح عليه». [٣]قوله : أكثر القدم ؛ قال في «الهداية» : «هو الصحيح».
And the emergence of most of the heel to the leg is removal (naz'). The wording of al-Quduri: 'most of the foot'. [1] His statement: 'It is appropriate'; by it he indicates that he did not find an explicit statement in that, but his principles necessitate it. [2] His statement: 'And the emergence of most of the heel' – with fatha on the 'ayn and sukun on the qaf, and also comes with kasr of the 'ayn with sukun of the qaf and fatha of the 'ayn with kasr of the qaf – meaning the back of the foot up to the place of the shoelace. Thus in Majma' al-Bihar. And in his mentioning it as a single term, it indicates that the emergence of most from one of them is also a nullifier, and this is if it is with the intention of removing the khuff. However, if it is not with the intention, then it does not invalidate the wiping by consensus. Thus in al-Nihayah. And in al-Muhit: 'If the khuff is wide such that when the foot is lifted, the heel rises, and when it returns it goes back to its place, there is no harm in wiping over it.' [3] His statement: 'most of the foot'; said in al-Hidayah: 'It is correct.'
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This is a memorization anchor stating a clear ruling: the emergence of most of the heel from the khuff (up to the shin) is legally equivalent to removing the khuff, thus invalidating the wiping. Al-Quduri's wording uses 'most of the foot' rather than 'heel'. The commentator explains the pronunciation of 'aqib (heel) and defines it as the back part of the foot to the place of the shoelace. The ruling applies even if only one heel (i.e., from one foot) comes out, but only if the person intends to remove the khuff. If there is no intention, the wiping remains valid by consensus. Furthermore, if the khuff is wide and the heel lifts temporarily but returns to its place, wiping is still valid. Al-Hidayah confirms that the correct criterion is 'most of the foot' (kathir al-qadam) coming out, which is the wording of al-Quduri.

Key Terms
العقب (al-‘aqib): The back part of the foot, up to where the shoelace lies.
النزع (al-naz’): Removal of the khuff; legally, exposing the foot invalidates the wiping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a wide khuff, the heel lifts when the foot is raised but returns when placed down. What is the ruling?
A) Wiping is invalidated because the heel was exposed.
B) Wiping remains valid because it was not intentional removal.
C) Wiping remains valid because the heel returned.
D) Wiping is invalidated if the heel was out for a moment.

Key Takeaway
The invalidation of wiping over khuffs due to exposure requires both emergence of most of the foot and intention to remove; temporary incidental exposure in a wide khuff does not nullify.

Determining When Wiping Over Khuffs Becomes Invalid
Ruling on invalidation of masah due to exposure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which wiping over khuffs becomes invalid and apply it to cases of intentional vs unintentional exposure.

Core Idea
Exposure of more than half the heel or foot with intent invalidates wiping.

Our passage from the commentary on al-Wiqayah clarifies an essential detail: exactly when wiping over khuffs is nullified. The scholars specify the minimum exposure required and distinguish between intentional removal and natural movement, along with an exception for loose khuffs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the invalidation (naz') of wiping over khuffs. Determine that the act is 'wiping over khuffs' and the ruling is that it becomes invalid (batil) under specific conditions.
2
Determine the measure of exposure
The matn says 'more of the heel' while al-Quduri says 'more of the foot'. Both are reconciled: exposure of more than half of either the heel or the foot counts.
The heel is defined as the back of the foot up to the thong of the khuff.
3
Distinguish intentional vs unintentional exposure
The invalidation occurs only if the exposure is done with the intention of removing the khuff. Unintentional exposure (e.g., due to loose fitting) does not invalidate by consensus.
Intention (niyya) is key.
4
Apply the exception for loose khuffs
If the khuff is wide and the heel naturally rises when lifting the foot and returns when placed back, wiping remains valid even if the heel appears exposed momentarily.
This is a practical concession to avoid hardship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وخروج أكثر العَقِبِ إلى الساق نَزْع ، ولفظ القُدُوري : أكثر القدم، [١]قوله : وينبغي ; أشار به إلى أنه لم يجد تصريحاً في ذلك، لكن قواعده تقتضيه. [٢] قوله : وخروج أكثر العقب ; - بفتح العين المهملة، وسكون القاف، وجاء كسر العين أيضاً مع سكون القاف وفتح العين مع كسر القاف - : مؤخّر القدم إلى موضع الشراك. كذا في مجمع البحار. وفي إيراده مفرداً إشارة إلى أن خروج الأكثر من أحدهما أيضاً ناقض، وهذا إذا كان بنية نزع الخف، أما إذا لم يكن بنيته فلا يبطل المسحُ إجماعاً، كذا في «النهاية»، وفي «المحيط»: «إذا كان الخف واسعاً بحيث إذا رفع القدم ارتفع العقب، وإذا رجع عاد إلى موضعه، فلا بأس بالمسح عليه». [٣]قوله : أكثر القدم ; قال في «الهداية» : «هو الصحيح».
And the emergence of more of the heel to the leg invalidates [wiping]. And the wording of al-Quduri: 'more of the foot'. [1] His saying: 'and it should' indicates that he did not find an explicit statement about that, but his principles necessitate it. [2] His saying: 'and the emergence of more of the heel' – with fath of the 'ayn and sukun of the qaf, and also with kasr of the 'ayn and sukun of the qaf, and with fath of the 'ayn and kasr of the qaf – means the back of the foot up to the place of the thong (shirak). As in Majma' al-Bihar. And his mentioning it singly indicates that the emergence of more from either of them also invalidates, and this is if it is with the intention of removing the khuff. But if it is not with his intention, then the wiping is not invalidated by consensus, as in al-Nihayah. And in al-Muhit: 'If the khuff is wide such that when he lifts the foot the heel rises, and when he returns it returns to its place, then there is no harm in wiping over it.' [3] His saying: 'more of the foot'; he said in al-Hidayah: 'It is the correct [view].'
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the sharh of al-Wiqayah. It addresses the condition under which wiping over khuffs (leather socks) becomes invalid. The matn (original text) states that if more than half of the heel emerges towards the leg, the wiping is nullified (naz'). The commentator explains that the wording of al-Quduri uses 'more of the foot' instead of 'more of the heel', but both are valid. The correct view, according to al-Hidayah, is that if more than half of either the heel or the foot is exposed with the intention of removing the khuff, the wiping becomes invalid. However, if the exposure is unintentional (e.g., due to a loose khuff), the wiping remains valid by consensus. Additionally, if the khuff is wide and the heel naturally rises when lifting the foot but returns when placed back, wiping is permitted. The ruling differentiates between intentional and unintentional exposure, and the measure is the majority of the part emerging (heel or foot).

Key Terms
العَقِب (al-'aqib): The heel of the foot, up to the place of the thong (shirak) of the khuff.
نَزْع (naz'): Removal or nullification of the wiping status; here it means the wiping becomes invalid.
القدم (al-qadam): The foot, specifically the front part in context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum amount of exposure that invalidates wiping over khuffs according to the correct view in this passage?
A) Exposure of any part of the foot
B) Exposure of more than half of the heel or foot
C) Exposure of the entire foot
D) Exposure of three small toes

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is invalidated if more than half of the heel or foot is exposed intentionally; unintentional exposure does not nullify it.

Wiping over Khuff vs. Tayammum When Fearing Cold
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wiping vs. tayammum when fearing cold from removing khuff.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling on wiping over khuff when fearing cold and explain the tarjih between the transmitted and researched positions.

Core Idea
Tayammum is not required; the transmitted ruling permits wiping over khuff despite hadath.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: when a person has a minor impurity while wearing khuffs and fears harm from removing them, should he wipe over the khuff or perform tayammum? The research of later scholars like Ibn al-Humam suggests tayammum, but the transmitted position from earlier authorities permits wiping. Al-Allamah Qasim explicitly dismisses the contrary research, making wiping the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the two options
A person has a hadath while wearing khuffs and fears cold if he removes them. The two options are: (a) wipe over the khuff, or (b) perform tayammum instead of wudu.
The fear of cold is a valid excuse for not removing the khuff.
2
Understand the argument for tayammum
The author of al-Bada'i argues that fear of cold does not prevent the transmission of hadath (sirayat al-hadath). Since the impurity spreads, the wiping over the khuff is invalid without a prior valid wudu; thus tayammum is necessary.
This is a rational (research-based) argument.
3
Examine the transmitted position for wiping
Despite the above reasoning, most authoritative texts (al-Kafi, al-Zayla'i, Qadikhan, etc.) state that wiping is allowed absolutely (without time restriction). This is the al-manqul (transmitted) position.
Some sources equate the khuff to a jabbirah (splint) in this context.
4
Note the tarjih by al-Allamah Qasim
Al-Allamah Qasim explicitly says: 'There is no regard for the research of our teacher Ibn al-Humam when it contradicts the transmitted position.' This resolves the dispute in favor of wiping.
This is a methodological principle: transmitted authority overrides independent reasoning (ra'y).
5
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon ruling for fatwa is that wiping over the khuff is permissible (mubah) when fearing cold. Tayammum is not required.
This is the majority Hanafi position from the later authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيلزمه العدول إلى التيمم بدلاً عن الوضوء بتمامه، ولا يحتاج إلى مسح الخف أصلاً مع التيمم حيث تحققت الضرورة المبيحة له..... والذي حققه في «البدائع» بحثا لزوم التيمم دون المسح ، فإنه بعـد مـا نقـل عـن جوامع الفقه» و«المحيط» أنه إن خاف البرد فله أن يمسح مطلقاً أي بلا توقيت . قال ما نصه : فيه نظر ، فإن خوف البرد لا أثر له في منع السراية ، كما أن . عدم الماء لا يمنعها، فغاية الأمر أنه لا ينزع ، لكن لا يمسح بل يتيمم لخوف البرد . اهـ وأقره في شرح المنية وأطنب في حسنه ; وهو صريح في انتقاض المسح لسراية الحدث، فلا يصلي به إلا بعد التيمم لا المسح. ولكن المنقول هو المسح لا التيمم كما مر عن الكافي» و «عيون المذاهب» و«الجوامع» ، وبه صرح الزيلعي وقاضي خان والقهستاني عن «الخلاصة»، وكذا في «التاتارخانية» و«الولوالجية» و«السراج» عن «المشكل» ، وكذا في «مختارات النوازل» لصاحب و«المحيط» الهداية ، وبه صرح أيضاً في «المعراج» و «الحاوي القدسي» بزيادة جعله كالجبيرة، وعليه مشى في «الإمداد». وقد قال العلامة قاسم : لا عبرة بأبحاث شيخنا يعني ابن الهمام إذا خالفت المنقول. فافهم».
So he must turn to tayammum instead of the complete wudu, and he does not need to wipe the khuff at all with tayammum when the necessity permitting it is realized. And what is verified in al-Bada'i by research is the necessity of tayammum without wiping. Because after quoting from Jami' al-Fiqh and al-Muhit that if he fears the cold, he may wipe absolutely, i.e., without time restriction, he said textually: 'There is consideration in it, for fear of cold has no effect in preventing the transmission [of hadath], just as lack of water does not prevent it. The most that can be said is that he does not remove [the khuff], but he does not wipe; rather he performs tayammum due to fear of cold.' End [quote]. And he approved it in Sharh al-Munyah and elaborated on its beauty; and it is explicit that wiping is invalidated by the transmission of hadath, so he cannot pray with it except after tayammum, not after wiping. However, the transmitted [position] is wiping, not tayammum, as mentioned in al-Kafi, 'Uyun al-Madhahib, and al-Jawami', and it was stated explicitly by al-Zayla'i, Qadikhan, and al-Qahistani from al-Khulasah, and likewise in al-Tatar Khaniyyah, al-Walwaljiah, and al-Siraj from al-Mushkil, and likewise in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil of the author of al-Hidayah and al-Muhit. And it was also stated explicitly in al-Mi'raj and al-Hawi al-Qudsi with the addition of making it like a jabbirah (splint). And al-Allamah Qasim said: 'There is no regard for the research of our teacher, meaning Ibn al-Humam, when it contradicts the transmitted [position].' So understand.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the case of a person who has a hadath (minor impurity) while wearing khuffs and fears that removing them will cause harm due to extreme cold. The initial opinion stated is that he must perform tayammum and not wipe over the khuff, because the hadath has already invalidated the wiping (since the khuff was not removed immediately? Actually, the idea is that the state of purity from wudu is lost, but since one cannot remove the khuff, one cannot wash the feet either. The research in al-Bada'i argues that fear of cold does not prevent the transmission of hadath (i.e., the impurity 'spreads' to the feet in the khuff?), so wiping cannot be valid; instead, one must do tayammum. However, the transmitted position (al-manqul) from many authorities (al-Kafi, al-Zayla'i, Qadikhan, etc.) is that one may wipe over the khuff absolutely, even without time restriction, because fear of cold makes it permissible. The commentator then cites al-Allamah Qasim who dismisses the research of Ibn al-Humam as contrary to the transmitted position. Therefore, the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is that one wipes over the khuff, not that one does tayammum. The phrase 'فافهم' indicates that this is a nuanced point but the final verdict is with the majority transmitted view.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu when water is not available or cannot be used.
خوف البرد (khawf al-bard): Fear of harm from cold, which may prevent removing the khuff for washing the feet.
سراية الحدث (sirayat al-hadath): Transmission of the state of ritual impurity; here it means that after a hadath, the impurity affects the entire body, making wiping invalid without prior removal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the transmitted position (al-manqul) in this passage, what should a person do if he has a hadath and fears cold from removing his khuff?
A) Perform tayammum and not wipe
B) Wipe over the khuff without time restriction
C) Remove the khuff and wash despite the cold
D) Repeat wudu with wiping

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi is that one wipes over the khuff when fearing cold, despite the alternative research.

Size of Hole in Khuff That Prevents Wiping
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the invalidation of wiping due to a hole in the khuff

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi narrations on the hole size that invalidates wiping and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A hole showing three smallest toes invalidates khuff wiping; other narrations differ on the measure.

Wiping over the khuff is a concession for travellers, but what if the khuff has a hole? This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explores the different narrations from Abu Hanifa and his students regarding the size of a hole that voids the wiping. The discussion distinguishes between measuring by toes for the hole and fingers for the act of wiping, based on the function of walking.

Guided Path
1
State the matn's ruling
Identify the explicit condition in the text: a hole showing three of the smallest toes of the foot prevents the validity of wiping.
This is the default ruling from Abu Yusuf's narration.
2
List the alternative narrations
Contrast the matn's ruling with other narrations from Abu Hanifa (top of foot measure, normal walking test) and the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
Note which imam each narration is attributed to.
3
Understand the talil (ratio legis)
Analyze why toes are used for the hole and fingers for wiping: walking is by foot, wiping by hand. The hole's effect on walking determines the measure.
This shows the madhhab's use of function-specific qiyas.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify which position is relied upon in fatwa: the precautionary opinion of three small toes, as chosen by the commentator and authorities.
This is the strongest position due to its conservatism and support in the sources.
