And a hole in the khuff from which appears the measure of three of the smallest toes of the foot prevents it. [1] His saying: 'narrated from Abu Hanifa' – al-Barjandi said in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Wiqayah: 'What is mentioned in the text is a narration from Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa. In another narration from him, if he takes out from the top of the foot the measure of three fingers, his wiping is invalidated. And in a narration: if it is such that he can walk after moving his foot from its place, then this does not prevent the permissibility of wiping, mentioned in al-Khulasah. And it is mentioned in al-Hisr that according to Abu Yusuf, as long as more of the top of the foot does not come out to the place of the leg, the wiping is not invalidated. And in al-Kafi: most of the mashayikh follow what is narrated from Muhammad, that if there remains on the top of the foot in the place of wiping the measure of three fingers, the wiping is not invalidated.' [2] His saying: 'yabdu' – meaning appears; it is a description of the hole, and the pronoun refers to it; i.e., a hole from which appears from the khuff the measure of three toes – with kasr of the ra'. And it can be a description of the khuff, and the pronoun also refers to it. [3] His saying: 'measure of three toes of the foot'; he said in al-Nihayah quoting from Mabsut Shaykh al-Islam: 'Consideration is given in the case of a hole to three toes of the foot, and in the case of wiping to three fingers of the hand. The difference between them is that if the hole is the measure of three fingers, it prevents the permissibility of wiping because it prevents the cutting of travel, and walking is only realized by the foot, so three toes of the foot are considered. As for the act of wiping, it is considered from the hand, so it is considered by the fingers of the hand.' The caution is against the emergence of less than the foot being a hardship as in a wide khuff, and there is no hardship for its majority, and the majority is treated as the whole. (1) So for him, the wiping remains because the place of washing remains in the khuff. And by the emergence of more of the heel to the leg, which is in the ruling of the apparent, the place of washing does not remain in it, and also, it is not possible with it to maintain normal walking. Al-Qari said in Fath Bab al-'Inayah: 'It is the most precautionary and the commentator chose it according to the saying of Abu Hanifa in al-Nuqayah, and the author of al-Fath and al-Bada'i.'

Commentary
This passage discusses the condition of a hole (kharq) in the khuff and its effect on the validity of wiping. The matn states that a hole that shows three of the smallest toes of the foot prevents the validity of wiping. The commentary explores different narrations from Abu Hanifa and the opinions of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to al-Barjandi, the text's ruling is a narration from Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa. There is another narration that if the hole is on the top of the foot and is of three fingers' width, wiping is invalidated. Yet another narration considers whether the foot can be moved normally for walking; if so, the hole does not prevent wiping. Abu Yusuf's condition is that more of the top of the foot must be exposed to the leg to invalidate. Muhammad's view is that as long as three fingers' width of the top of the foot remains in the wiping area, the wiping is valid. The passage then explains the difference between considering toes and fingers: for the hole, toes are considered because walking matters; for the act of wiping, fingers are considered because it is done by hand. Finally, the commentator notes that if more than half of the heel emerges, the wiping is invalid because no place for washing remains and normal walking is disrupted. The preferred view is that the hole of three toes prevents wiping, as chosen by the commentator and supported by Abu Hanifa's statement in al-Nuqayah.

Key Terms
خرق (kharq): A hole or tear in the khuff that exposes the skin.
أصابع الرجل (asabi' al-rijl): Toes of the foot; here specifically the three smallest toes.
أصابع اليد (asabi' al-yad): Fingers of the hand; used as measure for the area to be wiped.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Three fingers of the hand
B) Three smallest toes of the foot
C) The entire foot
D) More than half of the heel

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position: a hole in the khuff showing three of the smallest toes invalidates wiping; other narrations offer different thresholds but the precautionary view is preferred.

Conditions for Wiping over Khuffs: Holes and Their Measurement
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hole measurement and combination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on holes in khuffs, distinguish the main intra-madhhab positions, and apply the mashhur view that multiple holes are combined.

Core Idea
A khuff hole revealing three toes prevents wiping; smaller holes are overlooked due to hardship.

This lesson explores the conditions for valid wiping over khuffs, focusing on the impact of holes. The Hanafi school, recognizing that khuffs often have small tears, sets a threshold: only a hole revealing three of the smallest toes invalidates wiping. The passage also examines an intra-madhhab dispute on combining multiple holes and the rationale of avoiding hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Base Ruling
State the rule: a hole in the khuff that reveals three of the smallest toes of the foot prevents valid wiping. Note that this is the narration of Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa.
The measurement is specific to the foot, not the hand.
2
Map the Intra-Hanafi Disputes
List the different narrations from Abu Hanifa and the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the size and location of the hole. Understand how they differ on the threshold.
Muhammad's view (three fingers remaining on top) became the most followed.
3
Understand the Distinction in Measurement
Explain why the hole is measured by toes (for walking) while wiping is measured by fingers of the hand. This is a key point from the commentary.
Al-Nihayah clarifies the rationale: walking uses the foot, wiping uses the hand.
4
Analyze the Principle of Combining Holes
Describe the majority view (mashhur) that multiple holes on one khuff are combined; if total area equals three toes, wiping is invalid. Contrast with Ibn al-Humam's view of non-combination.
The author of al-Nahr al-Fa'iq notes the agreement of most texts and commentaries on combination.
5
Apply to Practical Cases
Use the examples from the text: a long hole that doesn't reveal the full amount, a hole that appears only when walking, and a split woven khuff. Determine validity in each case.
The key is whether the three-toe measure appears when the foot is at rest or when walking.

Book of Purification / Wiping over the Khuffs
And it is prevented by a hole in a khuff from which appears the measure of three of the smallest toes of the foot.
He chose in the text that it is narrated from Abu Hanifah.
(And it is prevented by a hole in a khuff from which appears the measure of three fingers of the foot, the smallest of them.
[1] His statement: narrated from Abu Hanifah – may Allah have mercy on him – al-Barjandi said in Sharh Mukhtasar al-Wiqayah: What is mentioned in the text is the narration of Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifah.
In another narration from him: If a measure of three fingers from the top of the foot is removed, his wiping is invalidated. And in a narration: If it is such that he can walk after his foot moves from its place, then this does not prevent the permissibility of wiping. Mentioned in al-Khulasa. And mentioned in al-Hasr: According to Abu Yusuf, as long as most of the top of the foot has not come out to the place of the leg, the wiping is not invalidated. And in al-Kafi: Most of the mashayikh follow what is narrated from Muhammad, that if three fingers' worth of the top of the foot in the place of wiping remains, the wiping is not invalidated.
[2] His statement: yabdu – i.e., appears from it. It is a description of the hole, and the pronoun refers back to it; i.e., a hole from which appears from the khuff a measure of three fingers of the foot – with kasra on the ra – and it can be a description of the khuff, and the pronoun also refers back to it.
[3] His statement: the measure of three fingers of the foot. He said in al-Nihayah, quoting from Mabsut Shaykh al-Islam: He considered in the case of the hole three fingers of the foot, and in the case of wiping three fingers of the hand.
The difference between them: The hole, if it is the measure of three fingers, prevents the permissibility of wiping because it prevents covering the foot during travel, and walking is only realized by the foot, so three fingers of the foot are considered. As for the act of wiping, it is only considered by the hand, so it is considered by the fingers of the hand.
As a precaution against the emergence of less than the foot causing difficulty, as in a wide khuff, and there is no difficulty for more of it, and treating the majority as the whole.
Not less than that. So if the hole is long, three fingers of the foot can fit into it but this amount does not appear, wiping is permissible. And if it is closed but opens when walking and this amount appears, it is not permissible.
So it is understood from this that what is made from yarn and the like, split below the ankle, if it covers the ankle with a thread or the like that is tightened after wearing so that nothing appears from it, it is like a non-split one. And if it appears, it is like a hole, so the mentioned measure is considered.
(And he combines the holes of a khuff)
[1] His statement: Not less than it – there is a dispute with al-Shafi'i and Zufar, based on the fact that since washing of what appears is obligatory even if it is little, washing the remainder also becomes obligatory.
Its answer: Khuffs are rarely free from small holes, so considering them would lead to difficulty in removal.
[2] His statement: So it is understood from it – i.e., from what we mentioned, for it is understood from the two issues that he mentioned that the consideration in the permissibility and impermissibility of wiping is based on the appearance of that preventing amount or its non-appearance while walking.
[3] His statement: So the mentioned measure is considered – i.e., if that amount appears from it, wiping is not permissible; otherwise, it is permissible.
[4] His statement: And he combines – meaning the holes are combined, and they are considered as preventive if the total reaches that amount.
[1] His statement: The holes of a khuff – i.e., the holes occurring in one khuff. Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir chose non-combination, and his student Ibn Amir Haj al-Halabi in Halbat al-Mujalli Sharh Munyat al-Musalli strengthened it, and the author of al-Bahr preferred it, but he mentioned before that combination is the well-known in the madhhab. And the author of al-Nahr al-Fa'iq said: 'The agreement of the majority of the texts and commentaries on it indicates its preference.'
(1) Fath al-Qadir (1:134). (2) Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (1:185).
(2)
(3) End quote from al-Nahr al-Fa'iq (1:120), and he also said: 'Because the principle is that a hole is absolutely preventive; since the one wiping is not wiping over the khuff, but because khuffs are rarely free from holes, especially the khuffs of the poor, we said: a small hole is overlooked, and we combined them into one to avoid difficulty, unlike two.'
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is an expansion of the ruling on wiping over khuffs, specifically the condition regarding holes. The passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute, discussing the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The base ruling: a hole in the khuff that reveals three toes of the foot prevents valid wiping. The text clarifies that the measurement is of the smallest three toes (اصغرها). The author notes that this ruling is narrated from Abu Hanifa via Abu Yusuf. However, other narrations exist: one says if three fingers' worth of the top of the foot is exposed, wiping is invalid; another says if the hole is such that walking is still possible, it does not prevent wiping. Abu Yusuf's view is that as long as most of the top of the foot has not come out to the leg, wiping is valid. Muhammad's view (followed by most mashayikh) is that if three fingers' worth of the top of the foot remains in the wiping area, wiping is valid. The text explains the distinction between measuring the hole with the foot (walking) and the hand (wiping). It then addresses the case of a long but non-revealing hole, and a hole that appears only when walking. An analogy is made to woven khuffs that are split below the ankle: if covered, they are like intact; if the covering fails, the hole rule applies. Finally, the text discusses combining multiple holes on one khuff: the majority view (especially in later texts) is that holes are combined and if the total reaches the measure, wiping is invalid. Ibn al-Humam chose non-combination, but the mashhur is combination. The objection of al-Shafi'i and Zufar (who would require washing even a small exposed area) is answered by the difficulty of avoiding small holes.

Key Terms
الخرق (al-kharq): A hole or tear in the khuff that exposes the foot.
ثلاث أصابع الرجل (thalath asabi' al-rijl): The measure of three of the smallest toes of the foot, used as the threshold for what prevents wiping.
الجمع (al-jam'): Combining multiple holes on one khuff and considering their total area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the measurement used to determine if a hole prevents wiping over khuffs?
A) Three fingers of the hand
B) Three of the smallest toes of the foot
C) The size of a dirham
D) Any visible exposure

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school overlooks small holes in khuffs (under three toes) to avoid hardship, and combines multiple holes on the same khuff; if the total reaches the threshold, wiping is invalid.

10 min
Wiping over a Splint: Ruling, Evidence, and Conditions
Commentary on the ruling and conditions of wiping over a splint

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over a splint, identify the primary hadith evidence, and apply the conditions that make it permissible or obligatory.

Core Idea
Wiping over a splint is wajib when removing it would harm, and it does not require the splint to be tied in a state of purity.

When a limb is injured and covered with a splint or bandage, the normal washing in wudu or ghusl may cause harm. Islamic law provides a concession: wiping over the splint instead of washing the injured area. This lesson examines the ruling, its evidence from the Sunnah, the conditions governing its permissibility, and the important intra-Hanafi difference on whether it is fard or wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
The act is wiping over a splint (jabirah) during purification. Determine its ruling: permissible, obligatory, etc. Note the definition of jabirah.
Jabirah includes any covering placed on a wound for treatment.
2
Examine the primary evidence
Analyze the hadith from Jabir narrated by Abu Dawood. Understand how the Prophet ﷺ indicated that wiping over a bandage suffices when water harms.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but it is the strongest evidence in this chapter.
3
Identify the conditions for permissibility
List the conditions: harm from washing/wiping the wound, or harm from removing the splint. Note that if one can wipe the wound itself without harm, that is obligatory and wiping over the splint is not allowed.
The splint need not be tied in a state of purity, unlike khuffs.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa holds it is wajib (not fard); the Sahibayn hold it is a practical fard (omission invalidates prayer). Understand the practical consequence.
The mufta bihi is that it is wajib, so prayer is valid but sinful if omitted without excuse.
5
Apply the ruling to scenarios
Consider cases: splint that falls off before healing vs. after healing; harm vs. no harm; ability to wipe the wound directly.
Use the conditions and the adopted position to determine the ruling.

كتاب الطهارة المسح على الخفين
ويجوز على جبيرة مُحدث
[2] (ويجوز على جبيرة مُحدث )
[1] قوله : ويجوز؛ أي المسح على جبيرة؛ الجبيرة – بفتح الجيم، وجمعه : جبائر، وهي العيدان التي تجبر بها العظام المكسورة، والتي تربط على موضع الكسر ونحوه؛ ليضم بعض الأعضاء إلى بعض والتحامها واتصالها.
والأصل في جوازه ما أخرجه أبو داود وهو أصح ما روي في هذا الباب عن جابر : «خرجنا في سفر فأصاب رجلاً منا حجر فشجه في رأسه، فقال لأصحابه: هل تجدون لي رخصة في التيمم، فقالوا: ما نجد لك رخصة وأنت تقدر على الماء، فاغتسل فمات، فلما قدمنا على رسول الله ﷺ خُبِّر بذلك، فقال: «قتلوه قتلهم الله، ألا سألوا إذ لم يعلموا، فإنما شفاء العي السؤال، إنما كان يكفيه أن يتيمم أو يشد على جرحه خرقة ثم يمسح عليها ويغسل سائر جسده». وأخرج الدارقطني بسند ضعيف جداً عن ابن عمر : «إن النبي ﷺ كان يمسح على الجبائر».
وأخرج الطبراني بسند ضعيف عن أبي أمامة : «إن النبي ﷺ لما رماه ابن قمئة يوم أحد رأيته إذا توضأ حل عصابته ومسح عليها».
وأخرج ابن ماجه بسند ضعيف عن علي قال : «انكسرت إحدى زندي فسألت النبي ﷺ فأمرني أن أمسح على الجبائر». كذا في «البناية شرح الهداية» للعيني.
[2] قوله : محدث؛ ظاهره أنه لا يجوز المسح على جبيرة الجنب والحائض والنفساء

ولا يبطله السقوط إلا عن برء
ولا يبطله السقوط إلا عن برء)، المسح على الجبيرة إن أضر جاز تركه، وإن لم يضر فقد اختلفت الروايات عن أبي حنيفة في جواز تركه، والمأخوذ أنه لا يجوز تركه.
ثم لا يشترط كون الجبيرة مشدودة على طهارة، وإنما يجوز المسح على أنه ليس كذلك كما هو مصرح في المعتبرات، إلا أن يقال : المراد بالمحدث أعم ممن به حدث أصغر، ومن به حدث أكبر.
أو يقال : المراد به جبيرة من به حدث، بأن لم يشدها على طهارة، وأشار به إلى أنه لا يشترط فيه شدها على الطهارة؛ لأن شدها غالباً يقع على العجلة والضرورة، فاشتراطها فيه مورث إلى الحرج، ولا كذلك مسح الخفين.
[1] قوله : المسح على الجبيرة ... الخ؛ قال في «المحيط» : «لو ترك المسح على الجبائر والمسح يضره جاز، وإن لم يضر لم يجز، ولا تجوز صلاته عندهما، ولم نجد في الأصل قول أبي حنيفة، وقيل : عنده يجوز تركه، والصحيح أنه واجب عنده وليس بفرض».
[2] قوله : ثم لا يشترط؛ لعدم وجود دليل يدل عليه، بخلاف مسح الخفين، فإنه وردت الأحاديث باشتراط لبسهما على طهارة.
[3] قوله : وإنما يجوز ... الخ؛ يعني جواز المسح على الجبيرة إنما هو إذا لم يكن ذلك الموضع الذي شدت عليه الجبيرة ولا على غسله، بأن كان الماء قادراً على مسح يضر الجرح غسلاً أو مسحاً، أو كان لا يضره لكن يضر حل الجبيرة في كل مرة، فإن كان قادراً على مسح نفس القرحة وجب عليه ذلك، ولم يجز المسح على الجبيرة لعدم الضرورة والحرج.
The Book of Purification: Wiping over Khuffs. And it is permissible to wipe over a splint for one who has minor impurity. [2] (And it is permissible to wipe over a splint for one who has minor impurity.) [1] His statement: 'And it is permissible' meaning wiping over a splint. Al-jabirah (splint) – with fatha on the jim, its plural is jaba'ir, and they are the sticks by which broken bones are set, and which are tied over the place of the fracture and the like, to bring the parts of the limbs together and for their fusion and connection. The basis for its permissibility is what Abu Dawood narrated, and it is the most authentic narration in this chapter, from Jabir: 'We set out on a journey and a stone hit a man among us, wounding his head. He said to his companions: Do you find any concession for me regarding tayammum? They said: We do not find any concession for you while you are able to use water. So he performed ghusl and died. When we came to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, he was informed of that, and he said: "They killed him, may Allah kill them! Why did they not ask when they did not know? Indeed, the cure for ignorance is to ask. It would have sufficed him to perform tayammum, or to tie a cloth over his wound, then wipe over it and wash the rest of his body."' And al-Daraqutni narrated with a very weak chain from Ibn Umar: 'The Prophet ﷺ used to wipe over splints.' And al-Tabarani narrated with a weak chain from Abu Umamah: 'When Ibn Qumay'ah threw him on the day of Uhud, I saw that when he performed wudu, he untied his bandage and wiped over it.' And Ibn Majah narrated with a weak chain from Ali: 'One of my forearms broke, so I asked the Prophet ﷺ, and he commanded me to wipe over the splints.' This is in al-Binayah Sharh al-Hidayah by al-Ayni. [2] His statement: 'one who has minor impurity'; its apparent meaning is that it is not permissible to wipe over a splint for the junub, the menstruating woman, or the woman in postpartum bleeding. And it is not invalidated by falling off except after healing. And it is not invalidated by falling off except after healing. Wiping over the splint: if it causes harm, it is permissible to leave it; and if it does not cause harm, then the narrations from Abu Hanifa differ regarding the permissibility of leaving it, and the adopted position is that it is not permissible to leave it. Then it is not a condition that the splint be tied in a state of purity; rather, wiping over it is permissible even if it is not so, as is explicit in the reliable texts, unless it is said that 'one who has minor impurity' is more general, including both one with minor impurity and one with major impurity. Or it is said that what is meant is a splint of one who has impurity, i.e., that he did not tie it in a state of purity, and he indicated by this that it is not a condition that it be tied in a state of purity, because tying it usually occurs in haste and necessity, so stipulating it would lead to hardship, unlike wiping over khuffs. [1] His statement: 'Wiping over the splint... etc.'; he said in al-Muhit: 'If one abandons wiping over splints and the wiping harms him, it is permissible; if it does not harm, it is not permissible, and his prayer is not valid according to them (the Sahibayn), and we did not find in the original (the statement of Abu Hanifa), and it is said that with him it is permissible to leave it, and the correct view is that it is obligatory (wajib) with him and not a fard.' [2] His statement: 'Then it is not a condition'; due to the absence of evidence indicating it, unlike wiping over khuffs, for the ahadith came stipulating that they be worn in a state of purity. [3] His statement: 'And it is permissible... etc.'; meaning the permissibility of wiping over the splint is only when that place upon which the splint is tied cannot be washed, i.e., water would harm the wound whether by washing or wiping, or it would not harm but removing the splint each time would harm. If one is able to wipe over the wound itself, that becomes obligatory upon him, and it is not permissible to wipe over the splint due to the absence of necessity and hardship.
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of wiping over a splint (jabirah) in the Hanafi school. The author begins by defining jabirah as the sticks or material used to set broken bones, tied over the fracture. The primary evidence is the hadith from Jabir where the Prophet ﷺ criticized those who did not ask for a ruling and stated that it would have sufficed to perform tayammum or to tie a cloth over the wound and wipe over it. This indicates the permissibility of wiping over a covering on a wound. Additional ahadith from Darqutni, Tabarani, and Ibn Majah are cited, though their chains are weak, but they support the ruling. The author then discusses the word 'muhdith' (one with minor impurity). The apparent meaning is that the ruling applies only to those with minor impurity, not to the junub, menstruating woman, or postpartum woman. However, later it is suggested that 'muhdith' might be general, including both types of impurity, or it might refer to one who tied the splint not in a state of purity. The condition that the splint be tied in a state of purity is not required, unlike wiping over khuffs, because tying a splint is often done in haste and necessity, and stipulating purity would cause hardship. The passage then addresses the issue of the splint falling off: it does not invalidate the wipe unless it falls off after the wound has healed. As for leaving the wipe: if wiping causes harm, it is permissible to leave it; if no harm, the narrations from Abu Hanifa differ, but the adopted position is that it is not permissible to leave it, and it is wajib (obligatory) but not fard according to Abu Hanifa, while according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is a practical fard such that if omitted, the prayer is invalid. Finally, the author clarifies when wiping over a splint is permissible: only when washing or wiping the wound directly would cause harm, or when removing the splint each time would cause harm. If one can wipe over the wound itself without harm, that is obligatory, and wiping over the splint is not permitted.

Key Terms
جبيرة (jabirah): The sticks or splints used to set broken bones, or the bandage tied over a wound or fracture.
محدث (muhdith): A person in a state of minor ritual impurity (hadath asghar).
برء (bur'): Healing of the wound; the point at which the splint is no longer medically necessary.
مسح (mash): Wiping with a wet hand over a body part or covering as a substitute for washing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on wiping over a splint when water would harm the wound?
A) It is permissible to leave it (no obligation to wipe).
B) It is obligatory (wajib) to wipe over the splint.
C) It is forbidden to wipe over the splint; one must wash the wound.
D) It is recommended (sunnah) but not required.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over a splint is a valid concession in purification when washing the wound would cause harm, and it is not conditioned on the splint being tied in a state of purity.

Wiping Over a Splint (Jabirah): Ruling and Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Explains ruling, intra-madhhab ikhtilaf, and purity condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over a splint, explain the difference between wajib and fard in this context, and identify why no condition of purity is required.

Core Idea
Wiping over a splint is wajib when direct washing harms, but unlike khuffayn, purity at tying is not required.

Wiping over a splint (jabirah) is a concession granted for wounds and fractures when direct washing or wiping would cause harm. However, the Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on whether this wiping is fard (invalidating prayer if omitted) or wajib (obligatory but not invalidating). Additionally, the conditions differ from wiping over leather socks (khuffayn) in a crucial way: purity at the time of tying is not required. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof, and the rationale behind these distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its basic ruling
The act in question is wiping over a medical splint (jabirah) during wudu or ghusl. Determine when it is permissible and when it is not.
The key condition is harm: if washing or wiping the wound directly harms, wiping over the splint is allowed; otherwise, it is not.
2
Examine the intra-madhhab dispute
Note the difference between Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Hanifa holds it is wajib (prayer valid but sinful if omitted), while they hold it is fard (prayer invalid if omitted).
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that of Abu Hanifa: wajib not fard.
3
Analyze the condition of purity
Unlike wiping over leather socks (khuffayn), the splint does not need to be tied while in a state of purity. The passage explains that this is because splints are applied in haste and necessity, and requiring purity would cause hardship.
This distinction is based on the principle of 'raf' al-haraj' (removal of hardship).
4
Understand the scope of the concession
The permission to wipe over the splint is limited to cases where one cannot wash or wipe the actual wound due to harm from water or from untying the splint. If one can wipe the wound directly, wiping over the splint is not allowed.
The harm can be direct (water hurts the wound) or indirect (untying the splint causes harm).
5
Connect to the dalil (proof)
The proof is based on qiyas (analogy) and the principle of harm removal (daran). The splint is treated like a wound covering that requires concession, similar to the case of a bandage, but with specific conditions.
The dalil is zanni (probable) because it is derived from general principles, not a specific text.

Source Text

قوله : المسح على الجبيرة ... الخ ؛ قال في «المحيط» (۱) : «لو ترك المسح على الجبائر والمسحُ يضرّه جاز، وإن لم يضرّ لم يجز، ولا تجوز صلاته عندهما، ولم نجد في الأصل قول أبي حنيفة ، وقيل : عنده يجوز تركه ، والصحيح أنه واجب عنده وليس بفرض (٢).
ثُمَّ لا يُشترط " كون الجبيرة مشدودة على طهارة ، وإنما يجوز المسح على مع أنه ليس كذلك كما هو مصرّح في المعتبرات ، إلا أن يقال : المراد بالمحدث أعم ممن به حدث أصغر، ومن به حدث أكبر.
أو يقال : المراد به جبيرة من به حدث، بأن لم يشدها على طهارة، وأشار به إلى أنه لا يشترط فيه شدّها على الطهارة ؛ لأنَّ شدّها غالباً يقع على العجلة والضرورة، فاشتراطها فيه مورث إلى الحرج، ولا كذلك مسح الخفين.
قال في «المحيط» (۱) : «لو ترك المسح على الجبائر والمسحُ يضرّه جاز، وإن لم يضرّ لم يجز، ولا تجوز صلاته عندهما، ولم نجد في الأصل قول أبي حنيفة ، وقيل : عنده يجوز تركه ، والصحيح أنه واجب عنده وليس بفرض (٢).
ثُمَّ لا يُشترط " كون الجبيرة مشدودة على طهارة ، وإنما يجوز المسح على مع أنه ليس كذلك كما هو مصرّح في المعتبرات ، إلا أن يقال : المراد بالمحدث أعم ممن به حدث أصغر، ومن به حدث أكبر.
أو يقال : المراد به جبيرة من به حدث، بأن لم يشدها على طهارة، وأشار به إلى أنه لا يشترط فيه شدّها على الطهارة ؛ لأنَّ شدّها غالباً يقع على العجلة والضرورة، فاشتراطها فيه مورث إلى الحرج، ولا كذلك مسح الخفين.
الجبيرة إذا لم يقدر على مسح ذلك الموضع من العضو، كما لا يقدر على غَسْلِه بأن كان الماء يضره، أو كانت الجبيرة مشدودة يضر حلها ، أما إذا كان قادرا على مسحه ، فلا يجوز مسح الجبيرة.
His statement: 'Wiping over the splint...etc.' He said in 'al-Muhit': 'If he leaves wiping over the splints and wiping would harm him, it is permissible; if it does not harm, it is not permissible, and his prayer is not valid according to them (the two companions), and we did not find in the original text the statement of Abu Hanifa, and it is said: according to him it is permissible to leave it, and the correct view is that it is obligatory (wajib) according to him and not an obligation (fard).' Then it is not a condition that the splint be tied while in a state of purity, and wiping is allowed even if it is not so, as is explicitly stated in the reliable works, unless it is said that 'the one in a state of minor impurity' (al-muhdith) is more general, including those with minor impurity and those with major impurity. Or it is said that it refers to the splint of one who is in a state of impurity, meaning he did not tie it while pure, and he indicated that it is not a condition that it be tied while in a state of purity, because tying it usually occurs in haste and necessity, so conditioning it causes hardship, and not so is wiping over leather socks. The splint: if he is unable to wipe that part of the limb, just as he is unable to wash it, because water would harm him, or because the splint is tied and untying it would harm him; but if he is able to wipe it, then wiping over the splint is not permissible.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof on the issue of wiping over a splint (jabirah). The author begins by citing al-Muhit, which states the basic ruling: if washing or wiping the wound directly would cause harm, then wiping over the splint is permissible. However, if there is no harm, then wiping over the splint is not permissible, and according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions), the prayer would be invalid without it. The text notes that the position of Abu Hanifa is not explicitly found in the original sources, but the preferred view is that it is wajib (obligatory) but not fard (essential) according to him. Then the author addresses the condition of the splint being tied while in a state of purity. Unlike wiping over leather socks (khuffayn), which requires that they be put on in a state of purity, no such condition is required for the splint because it is usually applied in haste and necessity, and requiring purity would cause hardship. The passage then defines the situation for wiping over the splint: it is only allowed when one cannot wash or wipe the actual wound due to harm from water or from untying the splint. If one can wipe the wound directly, then wiping over the splint is not allowed.

Key Terms
الجبيرة (al-jabirah): A splint or bandage placed on a wound or broken bone for treatment.
المحدث (al-muhdith): One who is in a state of minor ritual impurity (hadath asghar).
الخفين (al-khuffayn): Leather socks worn for warmth or protection, over which wiping is allowed in wudu under certain conditions.
رفع الحرج (raf' al-haraj): Removal of hardship; a principle in Islamic law that facilitates rulings in cases of necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on wiping over a splint when direct washing harms?
A) It is fard (obligatory, prayer invalid if omitted)
B) It is wajib (obligatory, prayer valid but sinful if omitted)
C) It is sunnah (recommended, no sin if omitted)
D) It is haram (forbidden)

Key Takeaway
Wiping over a splint is wajib when direct washing harms, and no purity condition is required for tying the splint, distinguishing it from wiping over leather socks.

The Ruling on Washing Cracks and the Dispute on Seeking Help
Intra-Hanafi dispute on seeking help with underlying capability principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequential ruling for washing cracks in wudu and explain the Hanafi intra-school dispute on whether seeking help is obligatory or recommended.

Core Idea
When washing a crack is harmful, pass water, wipe, then wash around; seeking help is recommended (Abu Hanifa) not obligatory (Sahibayn).

Wudu requires washing the limbs, but what if the skin has painful cracks? The Hanafi school provides a sequential alternative. Furthermore, if the person cannot perform wudu alone, should they seek help? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions differ. This lesson unpacks the rulings and the underlying principle of capability (qudrah).

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequential obligations for cracks
List the steps: if washing is harmful, pass water; if that is harmful, wipe; if wiping is harmful, wash around the crack. Each step is obligatory (wajib) only if the previous is impossible.
The sequence ends with leaving the crack dry, not with tayammum for that part.
2
Distinguish the positions on seeking help
Abu Hanifa holds that seeking help is mustahabb (recommended); if one does not seek help and does tayammum, prayer is valid. Sahibayn hold it is wajib (obligatory); prayer without it is invalid.
The same dispute applies to facing qiblah and moving from impurity.
3
Trace the underlying principle (qudrah)
Abu Hanifa: a person is capable only by his own means, not by another's. Sahibayn: capability can be established through another's assistance as an instrument.
Examples: son not obliged to accept father's money for Hajj; insolvent person not obliged to accept money for kaffarah.
4
Apply the principle to analogous cases
The text extends the dispute: if unable to face qiblah or move from impurity, Sahibayn require seeking help; Abu Hanifa does not.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's: seeking help is recommended, not obligatory. The text supports this by presenting his principle and examples.
Mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كان في أعضائه شقاق ، فإن عَجِزَ عن غَسْلِه ، يلزم إمرار الماء عليه ، فإن عَجِزَ عنه يلزمه المسح ، ثُمَّ إِن عَجِزَ عنه يغسلُ ما حوله ويتركه، وإن كان الشقاق في يده ويعجز عن الوضوء استعان بالغير ليوضئه.
[١] قوله : شقاق : بضمّ الشين، وعبارة غيره : شقوق ، بالضم ، وهو جمع الشق، وصـف عـارض للجلدِ بسبب البرد ونحوه ، يشق ويضر غسله، قال في «صحاح الجوهري»: «يقال : بيد فلان شقوق، وبرجليه شقوق، ولا يقال : الشقاق، وإنّما الشقاق داء يكون بالدواب ، وهي تَشقق به يصيب أرساغها، وبما ارتفع إلى أوظفتها).
[٢] قوله : استعان بالغير؛ قال في «المنية» وشرحه «الغنية»: «إن كان الشقاق في يده، وقد عجز عن الوضوء بنفسه يستعين بغيره ، حتى يوضئه استحباباً عند أبي حنيفة ، ووجوباً عندهما ، وإن لم يستعن وتيمَّمَ وصَلَّى جازت صلاته عند أبي حنيفة لله خلافاً لهما. وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا كان لا يقدر على الاستقبال أو على التحول عن النجاسة، ووجد من يوجهه ويحوّله ، تجب عليه الاستعانة عندهما لا عنده. والأصل : أن المكلف لا يعتبر قادراً بقدرة غيره عنده ؛ لأنَّ الإنسانَ إِنما يعد قادراً إذا اختص بحالة يتهيأ له الفعل متى أراد، وهذا لا يتحقق بقدرة غيره ؛ ولهذا إذا بذل الابن لأبيه المال والطاعة لا يلزمه الحج، ومن وجبت عليه كفارة وهو معسر فبذل له إنسان المال لا يجب عليه قبوله.
وعندهما تثبت له القدرة بآلة الغير ؛ لأنَّ آلته صارت كالته بالإعانة. كذا في «شرح الهداية ) للشيخ كمال الدین ابن الهمام (۳).
And if there are cracks (shiqaq) on his limbs, then if he is unable to wash them, it is necessary to pass water over them; if he is unable to do that, he must wipe them; then if he is unable to do that, he washes the area around it and leaves the crack. And if the crack is on his hand and he is unable to perform wudu by himself, he seeks help from another to perform wudu for him. [1] His statement: 'shiqaq' with a damma on the shin, and others express it as 'shuquq' with damma, which is the plural of shaqq, an affliction that occurs on the skin due to cold and the like, causing splitting and pain when washed. He said in 'Sihah al-Jawhari': 'It is said: So-and-so has shuquq on his hand, and shuquq on his feet, and it is not said: shiqaq; rather shiqaq is a disease that occurs in animals, which splits their pasterns and what is above their shanks.' [2] His statement: 'seeks help from another'; he said in 'al-Munyah' and its commentary 'al-Ghunya': 'If the crack is on his hand and he is unable to perform wudu by himself, he seeks help from another to perform wudu for him, as a recommended act according to Abu Hanifa, and obligatory according to them (the two companions). And if he does not seek help and performs tayammum and prays, his prayer is valid according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them. And the same disagreement applies if he is unable to face the qiblah or to move away from impurity, and finds someone to direct him and move him: it is obligatory upon him to seek help according to them, not according to him (Abu Hanifa). The principle is: according to him, the accountable person is not considered capable by the capability of someone else, because a person is only considered capable if he is in a situation where the action is available to him whenever he wishes, and this is not realized by someone else's capability. For this reason, if a son provides wealth and obedience to his father, he is not obliged to perform Hajj, and one who is obligated to pay kaffarah and is insolvent, if someone gives him money, he is not obliged to accept it. According to them, capability is established by the instrument of another, because his instrument becomes like his own capability through assistance. This is in 'Sharh al-Hidayah' by Sheikh Kamal al-Din Ibn al-Humam (3).
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage is an intra_hanafi_dispute concerning the ruling on performing wudu when one has cracks (shiqaq) on the limbs. The passage first outlines the sequential obligations: if washing the crack is harmful, one must pass water over it; if that is harmful, one must wipe; if even wiping is harmful, then wash around it and leave the crack. Then the text discusses seeking help: if the crack is on the hand and the person cannot perform wudu alone, he should seek help. However, there is disagreement: according to Abu Hanifa, seeking help is mustahabb (recommended), and if he does not seek help and instead performs tayammum and prays, his prayer is valid. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, seeking help is wajib (obligatory), and if he does not do so, his prayer is invalid. The same dispute applies to other situations like facing the qiblah or moving from impurity. The basis of the dispute is the principle of capability (qudrah): Abu Hanifa holds that a person is considered capable only if the action is available to him by his own means; capability via another's assistance is not considered true capability. The two companions hold that capability is established through the use of another as an instrument, as he becomes like an extension of himself. The passage provides examples to support Abu Hanifa's view: a son is not obliged to perform Hajj even if his father provides wealth, and an insolvent person is not obliged to accept money offered for kaffarah.

Key Terms
شقاق (shiqaq): Cracks on the skin due to cold or similar cause, making washing painful.
الاستعانة بالغير (al-isti'anah bil-ghayr): Seeking help from another person to perform an action one cannot do alone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what is the ruling on seeking help from another to perform wudu when one has cracks and cannot do wudu alone?
A) Wajib (obligatory); prayer invalid without it
B) Mustahabb (recommended); prayer valid without it
C) Haram (forbidden); one must use tayammum
D) Mubah (permissible); no preference

Key Takeaway
When washing cracks is harmful, the obligation reduces sequentially; and seeking help is recommended, not obligatory, so prayer with tayammum is valid according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Taharah — Purification

Wiping Over Splints and Bandages: The Hanafi Hierarchy of Purification
Rulings on dispensations for wounds and cracks in wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the four-step hierarchy for washing cracks (shiqāq) and state the Hanafi position on seeking help when one cannot perform wudu alone.

Core Idea
Necessity permits only what is needed: wash if possible, then pass water, then wipe, then wash around.

When a wound or skin condition makes washing a limb during wudu harmful, Islamic law provides a structured concession. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rulings on wiping over splints, bandages, and medicated areas, and examines a key principle: when does another person's assistance make you capable? Understanding this hierarchy and the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn is essential for correctly applying these dispensations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the medical condition
Determine whether the person has a splint (jabīrah), skin cracks (shiqāq), a bloodletting cloth, or medication. Each has a distinct ruling.
Cracks are due to cold; splints for fractures.
2
Apply the washing hierarchy for cracks
First attempt to wash gently; if harmful, pass water over without rubbing; if still harmful, wipe; if even wiping harms, wash around the area and leave the cracks.
This cascade minimizes harm while maintaining purity.
3
Analyze the splint ruling
If unable to wash or wipe the wound due to harm or difficulty removing the splint, wiping the splint itself is obligatory. But if the wound can be wiped directly, wiping the splint is impermissible.
The dispensation does not exceed the necessity.
4
Examine the help-seeking dispute
If a person cannot perform wudu alone due to cracks on the hand, Abu Hanifa says seeking help is recommended (not obligatory), while the Sahibayn say it is obligatory. The principle: capability is only one's own ability; another's help does not make one capable in the legal sense.
This difference affects the validity of tayammum if help is not sought.
5
Apply the bloodletting cloth ruling
After bloodletting (faṣd), wipe the cloth (khirqah) that directly touches the wound, not the outer bandage (ʿiṣābah), because the cloth is the actual barrier.
Some later authorities emphasize this distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجبيرة إذا لم يقدر على مسح ذلك الموضع من العضو، كما لا يقدر على غَسْلِه بأن كان الماء يضره، أو كانت الجبيرة مشدودة يضر حلها، أما إذا كان قادرا على مسحه، فلا يجوز مسح الجبيرة.
وإذا كان في أعضائه شقاق، فإن عَجِزَ عن غَسْلِه، يلزم إمرار الماء عليه، فإن عَجِزَ عنه يلزمه المسح، ثُمَّ إِن عَجِزَ عنه يغسلُ ما حوله ويتركه، وإن كان الشقاق في يده ويعجز عن الوضوء استعان بالغير ليوضئه،
[١] قوله: شقاق: بضمّ الشين، وعبارة غيره: شقوق، بالضم، وهو جمع الشق، وصـف عـارض للجلدِ بسبب البرد ونحوه، يشق ويضر غسله، قال في «صحاح الجوهري»: «يقال: بيد فلان شقوق، وبرجليه شقوق، ولا يقال: الشقاق، وإنّما الشقاق داء يكون بالدواب، وهي تَشقق به يصيب أرساغها، وبما ارتفع إلى أوظفتها). [٢] قوله: استعان بالغير؛ قال في «المنية» وشرحه «الغنية»: «إن كان الشقاق في يده، وقد عجز عن الوضوء بنفسه يستعين بغيره، حتى يوضئه استحباباً عند أبي حنيفة، ووجوباً عندهما، وإن لم يستعن وتيمَّمَ وصَلَّى جازت صلاته عند أبي حنيفة لله خلافاً لهما. وعلى هذا الخلاف إذا كان لا يقدر على الاستقبال أو على التحول عن النجاسة، ووجد من يوجهه ويحوّله، تجب عليه الاستعانة عندهما لا عنده. والأصل: أن المكلف لا يعتبر قادراً بقدرة غيره عنده؛ لأنَّ الإنسانَ إِنما يعد قادراً إذا اختص بحالة يتهيأ له الفعل متى أراد، وهذا لا يتحقق بقدرة غيره؛ ولهذا إذا بذل الابن لأبيه المال والطاعة لا يلزمه الحج، ومن وجبت عليه كفارة وهو معسر فبذل له إنسان المال لا يجب عليه قبوله. وعندهما تثبت له القدرة بآلة الغير؛ لأنَّ آلته صارت كالته بالإعانة. كذا في «شرح الهداية» للشيخ كمال الدین ابن الهمام. (انتهى من «غنية المستملي شرح منية المصلي»)
فإن لم يستعن وتيمم جاز خلافاً لهما.
وإذا وَضَعَ الدَّواء على شقاقِ الرِّجلِ أَمَرَّ الماء فوقَ الدَّواء، فإِذا أَمَرَّ المَاءَ فوق الدواء، ثُمَّ سَقط الدَّواء إن كان السقوط عن بُرْ، غَسَلَ الموضع وإلا فلا. وإذا فَصد، ووضع خرقة، وشَدَّ العصابة: فعند بعض المشايخ: لا يجوز المسح عليها، بل على الخرقة.
[١] قوله: خلافا لهما؛ فإن لم يجد من يوضئه أو وجده فاستعان به فأبى عن الإعانة فتيمم وصلّى جازت صلاته بلا خلاف، فتحقق العجز من كل وجه. [٢] قوله: وإذا وضع الدواء؛ كالمرهم أو الشحم أو نحوه. [3] قوله: إن كان؛ أي إن كان سقوط الدواء بسبب حصول البرء ودفع الحرج يلزمُ عليهِ غَسلَ ذلك الموضع، ولا يكفيه غير ذلك؛ لاندفاع الحرج، وإن كان سقوطه لا عن برء بل بسبب إمرارِ الماءِ وغيره لا يلزمُهُ الغَسل لبقاء العذر الآن كما كان. [٤] قوله: عن برء؛ كلمة عن مستعملة في مثل هذا الموضع بمعنى الباء، نحو قوله: وَمَا يَنطِقُ عَنِ المَوَى (٣)، أو بمعنى اللام نحو قوله: (وَمَا نَحْنُ بِشَارِكي وَالهَيْنَا عن قولك)، أو بمعنى بعد نحو قوله: عَمَّا قَليلٍ لَيُصْبِحُنَّ نَدِمِينَ (٥). [0]قوله: ووضع خرقة؛ أي على موضع الفصد، وهو بكسر الخاء المعجمة: القطعة من الثوب. [٦] قوله: وشد العصابة؛ أي على تلك الخرقة، وهو بالكسر ما يعصب ويشدّ من الثوب على الجراحة وعلى موضع الفصد ونحو ذلك. [۷] قوله: لا يجوز المسحُ عليها؛ لعل وجهه أنّ المتصل بالعضو إنما هو الخرقة، فتقوم مقامه في المسح لا العصابة حتى يكفي مسحها.
The splint: if he is unable to wipe that spot of the limb, just as he is unable to wash it either because water harms him or because the splint is tied tightly and untying it would harm him. But if he is able to wipe it, then it is not permissible to wipe the splint.
And if there are cracks (shiqāq) on his limbs: if he is unable to wash them, passing water over them is obligatory. If he is unable to do that, wiping is obligatory. Then if he is unable to do that, he washes around it and leaves it. And if the cracks are on his hand and he is unable to perform wudu on his own, he seeks assistance from another to perform wudu for him.
[1] The author's words: shiqāq: with a damma on the shīn. Others say shuqūq with a damma, plural of shaqq. It is an condition affecting the skin due to cold and the like, causing splits and making washing harmful. Al-Jawhari in his Ṣiḥāḥ said: "It is said: so-and-so has shuqūq on his hands and shuqūq on his feet, but one does not say shiqāq. Rather shiqāq is a disease that afflicts beasts of burden, causing splits in their pasterns and extending to their hocks." [2] The author's words: he seeks assistance from another; al-Munyah and its commentary al-Ghunyah said: "If the cracks are on his hand and he is unable to perform wudu by himself, he seeks assistance from another to perform wudu for him: it is recommended according to Abū Ḥanīfah and obligatory according to the two (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad). If he does not seek assistance and performs tayammum and prays, his prayer is valid according to Abū Ḥanīfah, contrary to them. On this same difference: if he is unable to face the qiblah or to move away from impurity, and he finds someone to direct him and move him, assistance becomes obligatory according to them but not according to him. The principle is: the legally responsible person is not considered capable by the capability of another, according to him, because a person is only considered capable when he has a condition in which the action is ready for him whenever he wishes, and this is not realized by another's capability. Hence, if a son offers his father wealth and obedience, Hajj does not become obligatory on him. And if atonement is obligatory on someone who is insolvent, and someone offers him money, acceptance is not obligatory. According to them, capability is established by another's means because his means become like his own through assistance. From Sharḥ al-Hidāyah by Kamāl al-Dīn Ibn al-Humām." (End quote from Ghunyat al-Mustamli Sharḥ Munyat al-Muṣallī)
If he does not seek assistance and performs tayammum, it is valid, contrary to them.
And if he places medication on the cracks of his foot, he passes water over the medication. When he has passed water over the medication, if the medication falls off due to healing, he washes that spot; otherwise, not.
And if he undergoes bloodletting, places a cloth, and ties a bandage: according to some teachers, it is not permissible to wipe over the bandage, but over the cloth.
[1] The author's words: contrary to them; if he does not find someone to perform wudu for him, or he finds him and seeks assistance but the person refuses assistance, then he performs tayammum and prays; his prayer is valid without dispute, because incapacity is established from all aspects. [2] The author's words: and if he places medication; such as ointment or fat or the like. [3] The author's words: if it is; meaning if the medication falls off due to the occurrence of healing and removal of hardship, then washing that spot is obligatory upon him, and nothing else suffices, because hardship is removed. But if it falls off not due to healing but due to passing water or something else, washing is not obligatory, because the excuse remains as it was. [4] The author's words: due to healing (an bar'); the word 'an is used in such a place meaning ba (as in: "and he does not speak from desire" [53:3]), or meaning lam (as in: "and we are not with you in sharing your gods after your saying" [11:53]), or meaning ba'd (as in: "after a little while they will become regretful" [23:40]). [5] The author's words: and placed a cloth (khirqah); on the spot of bloodletting; khirqah with a kasr on the khā' is a piece of cloth. [6] The author's words: and tied a bandage ('iṣābah); on that cloth; with a kasr, it is what is wound and tied from cloth on the wound or on the bloodletting spot and the like. [7] The author's words: it is not permissible to wipe over it; the reason is that what is attached to the limb is the cloth, so it takes its place in wiping, not the bandage, so that wiping the bandage would not suffice.
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings of wudu for those with medical conditions. It opens with the general rule regarding a splint (jabīrah): if the person is unable to wash the wounded area because water causes harm or because removing the splint would cause harm, then wiping over the splint is permissible. However, if they are able to wipe the actual wound area (e.g., the wound is exposed) without harm, then wiping the splint is not allowed; they must wipe the wound directly. This is based on the principle that necessity (ḍarūrah) permits only what is needed.
The text then addresses cracks (shiqāq or shuqūq) on the skin, which are splits caused by cold or similar conditions. When washing the cracks causes harm, the obligation progresses through steps: first, passing water over them (even if gently) is obligatory; if that harms, then wiping; if wiping harms, then washing around the affected area while leaving the cracks untouched. This hierarchy follows the principle of observing degrees of necessity.
A key intra-Hanafi dispute is presented on whether a person with cracks on their hand who cannot perform wudu alone must seek help from another. According to Imam Abū Ḥanīfah, seeking help is recommended (mustaḥabb) but not obligatory, because capability is defined by one's own ability, not another's. Therefore, if they do not seek help and instead perform tayammum and pray, their prayer is valid. The two companions (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) disagree, holding that seeking help is obligatory because another's assistance makes one capable, like using a tool. Thus, without seeking help, tayammum is invalid. The text provides the principle (aṣl) underlying Abū Ḥanīfah's view: a person is considered capable only if the action is ready for them whenever they wish, which is not achieved through another's power. Examples are given: a son offering wealth for Hajj does not obligate the father, and offering money for atonement to an insolvent person does not obligate acceptance. The companions' view is that assistance makes another's means like one's own.
The passage then covers a practical scenario: if medication is applied to cracked skin, water must be poured over the medication without rubbing. If the medication later falls off due to healing (indicating the wound is better), the underlying skin must be washed. If it falls due to the water itself, washing is not required as the excuse persists.
Finally, the ruling on bloodletting (faṣd) is given: after bleeding, a cloth is placed on the spot and a bandage tied over it. According to some later authorities (baʿḍ al-mashāyikh), it is not sufficient to wipe only the bandage; one must wipe the cloth directly, because it is the cloth that contacts the wound. The bandage is merely a cover. This distinction ensures that the wiping is over the actual barrier that necessitated the dispensation.

Key Terms
الجبيرة (al-jabīrah): A splint or cast placed on a broken bone or wound that cannot be removed easily.
الشقاق/الشقوق (al-shiqāq / al-shuqūq): Cracks or fissures in the skin caused by cold or dryness, making washing painful or harmful.
الفصد (al-faṣd): Bloodletting by opening a vein, typically for medical purposes.
الخرقة (al-khirqah): A piece of cloth placed directly on the wound or bloodletting spot.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person has skin cracks (shiqāq) on his foot and passing water over them is harmful, what is the next step in the hierarchy?
A) Wash the cracks thoroughly no matter what.
B) Wipe the cracks.
C) Wash around the cracks and leave them.
D) Perform tayammum instead of wudu.

Key Takeaway
When washing a wound in wudu causes harm, the Hanafi school provides a structured cascade of alternatives: wash gently, then pass water, then wipe, then wash around—each step only when the previous is harmful.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Tayammum without Seeking Help: Abu Hanifa vs. the Two Companions
Ruling on tayammum when help for wudu is not sought

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tayammum when help for wudu is available but not sought, and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two principal companions.

Core Idea
Tayammum is valid without seeking help only if help is unavailable or refused; seeking help is not an absolute condition.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling within the Hanafi school: is it permissible to perform tayammum when one could potentially get help to perform wudu? The base text (matn) declares it permissible, contradicting Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The commentary clarifies the boundaries of this dispute and identifies where consensus applies. Understanding this ruling sharpens your ability to apply the fiqh principle that necessity is measured by its extent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is performing tayammum when one does not seek help for wudu. The base text rules it as permissible (jāza). This is the Hanafi position of Imam Abu Hanifa.
The ruling is opposed by the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad).
2
Locate the proof (dalīl)
The commentator provides the proof: when inability (‘ajz) is absolute – no helper found or helper refuses – there is consensus (ijmā‘) that tayammum is valid. The disagreement only arises when help is available but not sought.
The proof relies on the concept of complete inability (al-‘ajz min kulli wajh).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalālah
The legal link is that tayammum is a substitute for wudu allowed only when wudu is impossible. If one can delegate wudu to another, wudu becomes possible, so tayammum would not be allowed according to the two companions. Abu Hanifa argues that imposing on another is not obligatory; inability remains if one does not wish to burden others.
This is a difference in evaluating what constitutes true inability.
4
Note the ikhtilāf
The two companions require seeking help as a condition before tayammum, because they consider the ability to delegate as removing the inability. Abu Hanifa treats delegation as a voluntary act, not an obligation.
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement (ikhtilāf al-madhhab).
5
Evaluate the tarjīḥ
The relied-upon position (muftā bihī) in the Hanafi school is the view of Abu Hanifa. The commentary emphasizes that when inability is complete, there is no dispute at all.
The later Hanafi masters prefer Abu Hanifa's position because it avoids hardship and compulsion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن لم يستعن وتيمم جاز خلافا لهما. [۱] قوله : خلافا لهما ; فإن لم يجد من يوضئه أو وجده فاستعان به فأبى عن الإعانة فتيمم وصلّى جازت صلاته بلا خلاف، فتحقق العجز من كل وجه.
If he does not seek help and performs tayammum, it is permissible, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). [1] His saying: 'contrary to the two'; for if he does not find anyone to perform wudu for him, or he finds someone but he refuses to help, so he performs tayammum and prays, his prayer is valid without disagreement, because inability is realized from all aspects.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The base text states a position: if a person who is unable to perform wudu himself does not seek help from others to perform wudu for him, and instead does tayammum, it is valid. This is contrary to the view of Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two companions of Abu Hanifa). The commentator explains that the ruling is actually agreed upon when the person truly cannot find anyone to help, or finds someone but they refuse. In that case, tayammum is valid without any disagreement because the inability is complete. This clarifies that the disagreement only applies when help is available but not sought.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
عجز ('ajz): Inability to perform wudu due to lack of water or a helper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, when is tayammum valid without any disagreement (bilā khilāf)?
A) When the person intentionally refuses to seek help
B) When the person cannot find a helper or the helper refuses
C) Only when water is completely unavailable
D) When the person is traveling

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is valid without seeking help according to Abu Hanifa, but the two companions require seeking help; the relied-upon opinion is Abu Hanifa's.

Washing the Wound When Medicine Falls Off After Healing
Ruling on washing wound site when medicine falls after healing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition that triggers the obligation to wash the wound site when medicine falls off after wudu, and state the Hanafi ruling for each scenario.

Core Idea
Only healing, not water, triggers washing the wound site when medicine falls off.

When performing wudu with a medicated wound, a common question arises: after the medicine falls off, must you wash that spot? The Hanafi ruling distinguishes between falling due to healing and falling due to the water itself. This lesson unpacks that conditional rule and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is placing medicine on a crack and then performing wudu by passing water over it. When the medicine later falls off, the ruling depends on the cause of the fall. Determine the two possible rulings: washing required or not required.
The base ruling is conditional, not absolute.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
If the medicine falls because the wound has healed (bur'), then washing the site is obligatory. If it falls due to the water of wudu or any other non-healing cause, washing is not obligatory because the excuse (the wound) persists.
The key distinction is the cause: healing vs. non-healing.
3
Understand the basis for the distinction
When the wound is still present, the difficulty (haraj) of washing remains, so the concession of wiping over the medicine continues. Once healed, the difficulty is removed and the original obligation to wash returns.
The underlying principle is removal of hardship (raf' al-haraj).
4
Apply the ruling to a concrete case
Take a person with a cracked foot who applies ointment and performs wudu. If later the ointment falls off and the crack is healed, he must wash that spot in his next wudu. If not healed, he may continue wiping over any new medicine or wash if convenient.
The ruling applies each time wudu is performed after the ointment falls.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا وضع الدواء على شقاق الرجل أمر الماء فوق الدواء، فإذا أمر الماء فوق الدواء، ثم سقط الدواء إن كان السقوط عن برء، غسل الموضع وإلا فلا. [۲] قوله : وإذا وضع الدواء ; كالمرهم أو الشحم أو نحوه. [3] قوله : إن كان ; أي إن كان سقوط الدواء بسبب حصول البرء ودفع الحرج يلزم عليه غسل ذلك الموضع، ولا يكفيه غير ذلك; لاندفاع الحرج، وإن كان سقوطه لا عن برء بل بسبب إمرار الماء وغيره لا يلزمه الغسل لبقاء العذر الآن كما كان. [٤] قوله : عن برء ; كلمة عن مستعملة في مثل هذا الموضع بمعنى الباء، نحو قوله: وما ينطق عن الهوى، أو بمعنى اللام نحو قوله: وما نحن بمشركي // والمهينا عن قولك، أو بمعنى بعد نحو قوله: عن قليل ليصبحن نادمين.
And if he places medicine on cracks of the foot, [then] he passes water over the medicine, then if the medicine falls off, if its falling is due to healing, he washes the site; otherwise not. [2] His saying: 'And if he places medicine'; like ointment or fat or similar. [3] His saying: 'if its falling is'; i.e. if the falling of the medicine is due to the occurrence of healing and the removal of difficulty, then washing that site is necessary, and nothing else suffices; because the difficulty is removed. And if its falling is not due to healing but due to the passing of water etc., then washing is not necessary due to the persistence of the excuse as it was. [4] His saying: 'due to healing'; the word 'an' is used in such contexts in the sense of 'ba' (with), as in His saying: 'And he does not speak from desire'; or in the sense of 'lam' (for), as in His saying: 'And we are not associates ...'; or in the sense of 'ba'd' (after), as in His saying: 'After a little while they will become regretful.'
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with commentary. The base ruling: if a person has a medical ointment on cracks of his feet and performs wudu by passing water over it, if the ointment later falls off, he must wash that spot only if it fell due to healing. If it fell due to the water, he need not wash because the excuse persists. The commentator explains the type of medicine, the condition of falling, and provides a linguistic analysis of the word 'an' used here. This ruling applies to wudu when there is a wound or crack with medicine.

Key Terms
شقاق (shiqāq): Cracks or fissures in the skin, especially of the feet.
برء (bur'): Healing or recovery from the wound/crack.
إمرار الماء (imrār al-mā'): Passing of water (over the medicine).
حرج (ḥaraj): Difficulty, hardship, or constraint.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, when is it obligatory to wash the wound site after the medicine falls off?
A) Whenever the medicine falls off, regardless of cause
B) Only if the medicine falls off due to healing
C) Only if the medicine falls off due to water
D) Only if the wound is still visible

Key Takeaway
The obligation to wash a wound site after medicine falls off depends on the cause: healing requires washing, else the excuse persists.

Wiping over the Bandage: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wiping over bandage during wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on wiping over a bandage for a phlebotomy wound and apply the principle of harm to determine the ruling.

Core Idea
If untying harms the wound, wipe over the bandage; necessity limits the ruling.

The passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether wiping over the outer bandage suffices or one must wipe directly on the cloth under it. Three positions emerge, each based on different considerations: ability, harm, and the extent of the bandage. We will navigate these positions and see how later Hanafi scholars settled the matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Understand the core question: When a person has a phlebotomy wound covered by a cloth (khirqa) and then a bandage (isaba), does wiping over the bandage fulfill the obligation of wiping the wound, or must he untie the bandage and wipe the cloth directly?
The base text states some mashayikh forbid wiping over the bandage.
2
Position 1: Based on ability (Abu Ali al-Nasafi)
If the person can untie the bandage and wipe the cloth without help, wiping over the bandage is invalid. If he cannot, the bandage takes the place of the cloth. This relies on Abu Hanifa's principle that ability with help is not considered.
This position focuses on the ability to perform the wiping directly.
3
Position 2: Based on harm (Ala al-Din Mahmud al-Sha'bi)
The consideration is the actual harm to the wound. If untying and wiping the cloth harms the wound, wiping over the bandage is permissible; otherwise not. This is the relied-upon position.
This aligns with the principle 'al-taklif bi hasab al-wus'' (obligation according to capacity).
4
Position 3: Based on extent of bandage (Khwahir Zade)
If the bandage extends beyond the wound, the same ruling applies: if washing the wound harms, wipe the whole bandage; otherwise wash the sides and wipe over the wound itself or the cloth if needed.
This applies the maxim 'what is established by necessity is limited to its extent.'
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi works (al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, Tabyin al-Haqa'iq) prefer the second position (based on harm). The operative ruling: if untying causes harm, wipe over the bandage; otherwise wipe the cloth.
The first position is also considered but the second is more comprehensive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا فصد ووضع خرقة وشد العصابة : فعند بعض المشايخ : لا يجوز المسح عليها، بل على الخرقة. [۱] قوله : لا يجوز المسحُ عليها ; لعل وجهه أنّ المتصل بالعضو إنما هو الخرقة، فتقوم مقامه في المسح لا العصابة حتى يكفي مسحها. [۲] قوله : إن أمكنه ; أي إن كان يمكن منه أن يحلّ العصابة فيمسح على الخرقة التي تحتها، ثم يشدها من غير إعانة أحد لا يجوز له المسح على العصابة ; لعدم الحرج حينئذ في حلها، وإمكان المسح على الخرقة. وإن لم يمكنه ذلك جاز المسحُ عليه، إذ لا معتبر بالقدرة على الشيء بإعانة الغير عند أبي حنيفة ، فعدم إمكانه حلّها وشدّها بدون الإعانة يثبت العجز عن المسح على الخرقة، فتقومُ العِصابة مقامها ، وفيه خلافٌ لهما على نحو ما مرَّ في مسألة الشقوق. [۳] قوله : وقال بعضهم ... الخ ; حاصلُ هذا القول أنّ العبرة في هذا الباب للضرر والحرج ; فإن كان حَلُّ العصابة ومسحُ الخرقة لا يضر الجراحة، لم يجز المسح على العصابة، وإن كان ذلك مضراً بها جاز المسحُ عليها ; لأنَّ التكليف بحسب الوسع ، ولو التصقت العصابة بالمحل بحيث يعسر نزعها جاز المسحُ أيضاً، ولو كان بعد البرء، لكن حينئذ يمسحُ على الملتصق ويغسلُ ما قدر على غسله من الجوانب. [٤] قوله : وكذا الحكم ; أي مثلُ الحكم في عصابة المفتصد ; فإذا كانت زائدة عن موضع الجراحة فإن ضره الحل والغَسل مسح الكلّ ، وإلا يغسل ما حول الجراحة ويمسح عليها لا على الخرقة ما لم يضره مسحها، فإن ضر يمسح على الخرقة التي عليها، ويغسلُ حواليها، وما تحت الخِرقة الزائدة ; لأنَّ الثابت بالضرورة يتقدر بقدرها. كذا فصله في «البحر الرائق» وغيرها.
And if he undergoes phlebotomy and places a cloth and ties a bandage: according to some mashayikh: wiping over the bandage is not permissible, but rather over the cloth. [1] His saying: 'wiping over it is not permissible'; perhaps its reason is that what is directly attached to the limb is only the cloth, so it stands in place [of the limb] for wiping, not the bandage, so that wiping it suffices. [2] His saying: 'if he is able'; i.e. if he is able to untie the bandage and wipe over the cloth underneath, then tie it without the help of anyone, then wiping over the bandage is not permissible for him; because there is no difficulty in untying it then, and it is possible to wipe over the cloth. And if he cannot do that, then wiping over it is permissible, because ability with the help of others is not considered according to Abu Hanifa. So his inability to untie and tie without help establishes his inability to wipe over the cloth, so the bandage takes its place. And there is a disagreement of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) similar to that which passed in the issue of cracks. [3] His saying: 'And some said...' the summary of this statement is that the consideration in this chapter is for harm and difficulty. So if untying the bandage and wiping the cloth does not harm the wound, then wiping over the bandage is not permissible. And if that is harmful to it, then wiping over it is permissible; because the obligation is according to capacity. And if the bandage adheres to the site such that removing it is difficult, then wiping over it is also permissible, even after healing, but then he wipes over the adhered part and washes what he can from the sides. [4] His saying: 'And the same ruling'; i.e. like the ruling regarding the bandage of the one who underwent phlebotomy. So if it exceeds the wound site, and untying and washing harms him, he wipes the whole bandage. Otherwise, he washes around the wound and wipes over the wound itself, not over the cloth, unless wiping it harms him. Then if it harms, he wipes over the cloth that is on it, and washes around it and what is under the excess cloth; because what is established by necessity is limited to its extent. Thus it is detailed in 'Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' and others.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding wiping over a bandage during wudu when one has a phlebotomy wound. The base text states that according to some Hanafi mashayikh, wiping over the outer bandage is not allowed; one must wipe directly on the cloth under it. The commentary then presents three positions:
1. The first position (attributed to Abu Ali al-Nasafi) holds that if the person can untie the bandage and wipe over the underlying cloth without needing help, he must do so; if he cannot, he may wipe over the bandage. This is based on Abu Hanifa's principle that ability with another's help is not considered.
2. The second position (attributed to Ala al-Din Mahmud al-Sha'bi) considers actual harm: if untying harms the wound, wiping over the bandage is allowed; otherwise not.
3. The third position (from Khwahir Zade) extends the same ruling to any cloth that extends beyond the wound: the consideration is the difficulty of washing underneath. The ruling is finalized in later works like Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, where the principle 'what is established by necessity is limited to its extent' is applied.
This shows how Hanafi scholars derive rulings based on the core principle of removing hardship (raf' al-haraj).

Key Terms
فصد (fasd): Phlebotomy or bloodletting from a vein, a medical procedure.
خرقة (khirqa): A piece of cloth placed directly on the wound or incision.
عصابة (isāba): A bandage used to wrap and secure the cloth over the wound.
حرج (haraj): Difficulty or hardship that is considered in determining the ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the text, when is wiping over the bandage permissible?
A) If the person cannot tie it without help
B) If untying and wiping the cloth harms the wound
C) Only if the bandage is made of cotton
D) Never

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, wiping over a bandage is permissible when removing it would cause harm to the wound; this is derived from the principle of removing hardship.
