Age of Menopause and Ruling on Blood After It
Intra-Hanafi dispute on post-menopausal bleeding

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi views on the age of menopause and apply the distinction between 'asahh' and 'mukhtar' rulings to determine whether blood after menopause is considered menstruation, and state the practical consequence on iddah.

Core Idea
The most correct view limits menstruation to menopause; the chosen view considers strong blood after menopause as menstruation — they are not contradictory.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: when a woman passes the age of menopause and sees blood, is it menstruation or not? The source text presents two terms — 'asahh' (most correct) and 'mukhtar' (chosen) — and resolves the apparent contradiction. Understanding this nuance is essential for correctly applying rulings on iddah, prayer, and sexual intercourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two views
The passage states the 'asahh' view: menstruation is temporally limited to the age of menopause, so blood after that is not menstrual. The 'mukhtar' view: strong blood after menopause is considered menstruation.
These are both Hanafi positions; the difference is intra-madhhab.
2
Understand the terms 'asahh' and 'mukhtar'
'Asahh' indicates the more correct general rule, while 'mukhtar' indicates the preferred view for fatwa, often used for exceptions. Recognize that they serve different functions.
Both are terms of tarjih (preference) in Hanafi literature.
3
Resolve the apparent contradiction
The commentator explains: 'asahh' refers to the temporal limitation itself — the general rule that menstruation ends at menopause. 'Mukhtar' refers to the exceptional case of strong blood, which is still menstrual. There is no contradiction because the general rule accommodates an exception.
This distinction allows both to be fatwa-worthy.
4
Recognize the age of menopause
The passage reports different opinions: 55 or 60 years, with some considering relatives or constitution. The fatwa in the author's time is on 55 years.
Modern medical knowledge may affect this, but Classical Hanafi fatwa is relied upon.
5
Apply the practical effect on iddah
If a divorcée thought she was menopausal and began a month-based iddah, but then strong blood returns during those months, the iddah is invalidated and she must restart with three menses. If blood returns after completion, the iddah stands.
This is the chosen (mukhtar) view according to al-Nahr and al-Mujtaba.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الأصح أن الحيض مؤقت إلى سن الإياس، فإذا بلغت المرأةُ ذلك السنّ ورأت الدم بعده لا يعد ذلك حيضاً. فإن قلت: هذا الذي ذكره من الأصح يدلّ على أن ما خرج بعد سن الإياس ليس بحيض مطلقاً، وهو منافٍ لما وسمه بلفظ : «المختار» مـن أن الـدم الـقـوي بعـده حيض، ومن المعلوم أن المختار والأصح كلاهما من ألفاظ الفتوى ، فكيف يصح جعلُ كل مفتی به، مع تخالفهما؟
قلت : الأصحية راجعة إلى نفس التوقيت لا إلى إطلاق الحيض، فلا تنافي، وللناظرين هاهنا كلمات بينا ما لها وما عليها في «السعاية».
[1] قوله : وأكثر المشايخ ... الخ ؛ قال العَيْني في «البناية»: «اختلف في زمان الإياس : فقيل : ستون، وعن محمد الله» في «المولدات»: ستون، وفي «الروميات»: خمس وخمسون ، وقيل : يعتبر أقرانها من قرابتها ، وقيل : يعتبر تركيبها ؛ لاختلاف الطبائع باختلاف البلدان ، وقيل : خمس وخمسون، والفتوى في زماننا عليه».
[2] قوله : ويبطل ؛ يعني لو طلقت الآيسة فاعتدت بالأشهر بناءً على أنّ عدة الآيسة ثلاثة شهور ثم عاد دمها قوياً، فإن كان ذلك في أثناء تلك الأشهر يحكم ببطلان تلك العدة، ويجب عليها استئناف العدة بثلاثة حيض ؛ لتبين كونها ذات حيض، وإن كان ذلك بعد تمام الأشهر الثلاثة لا يحكم ببطلانها، حتى لو نكحت زوجاً آخر بعد ثلاث أشهر لا يفسد ذلك النكاح. نعم يجب عليها العدة في المستقبل بالحيض، وهذا التفصيل هو الذي اختاره في «النهر» وقال: «هو أعدلُ الروايات»، وفي المجتبى»: «إنّه الصحيحُ المختار».
Then the most correct (asahh) is that menstruation is limited to the age of menopause. When a woman reaches that age and sees blood after it, that is not considered menstruation. If you say: This that he mentioned as 'most correct' indicates that what exits after the age of menopause is absolutely not menstruation, and it contradicts what he labeled 'the chosen' (mukhtar) that strong blood after it is menstruation. It is known that 'mukhtar' and 'asahh' are both terms of fatwa. How can each be made fatwa-worthy while they contradict each other? I say: 'Asahh' pertains to the temporal limitation itself, not to the absolute ruling of menstruation, so there is no contradiction. The commentators have words here; we have explained their pros and cons in 'al-Sa'ayah'. [1] His saying: 'And most of the scholars...' etc. al-Ayni said in al-Binayah: 'There is disagreement regarding the age of menopause: some say sixty, and from Muhammad (?) in al-Mawlidat: sixty, and in al-Rumiyyat: fifty-five, and it is said: consider her peers from her relatives, and it is said: consider her constitution due to difference of natures by country, and it is said: fifty-five, and the fatwa in our time is upon it.' [2] His saying: 'And it invalidates' – meaning if a menopausal woman is divorced and she observes her iddah by months based on the fact that the iddah of a menopausal woman is three months, then her blood returns strongly, then if that is during those months, it is ruled that the iddah is invalid, and she must restart the iddah with three menses because it is clarified that she is a menstruating woman. If that is after completion of the three months, it is not ruled invalid, such that even if she marries another husband after three months, that marriage is not invalidated. Yes, she must observe iddah in the future with menses. This detail is what was chosen in al-Nahr and he said: 'It is the most moderate of the narrations,' and in al-Mujtaba: 'It is the correct and chosen.'
Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on menstruation after the age of menopause (sin al-iyas). The base text stated that menstruation is limited to the age of menopause, meaning that blood after that age is not menstrual. However, there is another view (al-mukhtar) that strong blood (like black or bright red) is still considered menstruation. The commentator resolves the apparent contradiction: 'asahh' refers to the temporal limit itself (i.e., that menstruation generally ends at menopause), while 'mukhtar' refers to the exceptional case of strong blood. The passage then notes that most scholars set the age of menopause at fifty-five or sixty, with fatwa on fifty-five. Finally, it discusses the practical effect on iddah: if a woman thought she was menopausal and began a month-based iddah, but then her blood returns strongly, if it returns during the months, her iddah is invalid and she must restart with three menses; if it returns after completion, the iddah stands and her subsequent marriage is valid. This is the adopted view.

Key Terms
الإياس (al-iyas): The age at which a woman ceases to menstruate; the age of menopause.
الأصح (al-asahh): 'Most correct' – a term of preference in Hanafi fiqh, indicating a stronger view on the general rule.
المختار (al-mukhtar): 'The chosen' – a term indicating a preferred view, here referring to the exceptional ruling that strong blood after menopause is menstrual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman who is believed to be menopausal begins a month-based iddah, but then her blood returns strongly half way through, what happens to her iddah?
A) Her iddah continues and is valid.
B) Her iddah is invalidated and she must restart with three menses.
C) She must combine both months and menses.
D) She is considered still menopausal, so the blood is ignored.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves the tension between the general rule (menstruation ends at menopause) and the exception (strong blood after menopause is menstrual) by applying the exception when the blood is strong, affecting iddah and other rulings.

Age of Menopause and Its Effect on 'Iddah
Determining the age of menopause and subsequent bleeding effect on 'iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the age of menopause and explain the effect of subsequent bleeding on 'iddah.

Core Idea
Menopause age is disputed (55 vs 60), but strong blood after presumed menopause still counts as menstruation and invalidates month-based 'iddah.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'āyah addresses a key fiqh question: When does a woman definitively enter menopause such that her waiting period ('iddah) shifts from menstrual cycles to months? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on the exact age, and the ruling depends on the nature of the blood seen. Understanding this issue is crucial for correctly determining 'iddah and purity rulings for older women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the age dispute
Note the two main positions: most mashāyikh set it at sixty years, while the mashāyikh of Bukhārā and Khawārizm set it at fifty-five years. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The dispute is within the Hanafi school; both positions are valid opinions.
2
Understand the chosen view (mukhtār)
The chosen view for fatwa is 55 years, but more importantly, the quality of blood matters. Strong blood (black or deep red) indicates menstruation even after the presumed age of īyās.
This nuance resolves many practical cases.
3
Distinguish apparent madhhab vs chosen view
The apparent madhhab (ẓāhir al-madhhab) holds that any blood after īyās is not menstruation. However, the later chosen view (mukhtār) considers strong blood as menstrual.
The commentary clarifies that the dispute is about timing, not the definition of menstruation.
4
Apply the ruling on 'iddah
If a menopausal woman begins her 'iddah by months and then sees strong blood during those months, the month-based 'iddah is invalidated and she must observe 'iddah by three menstrual cycles. If the blood appears after the months are complete, the 'iddah is valid and she need not repeat it, but future 'iddahs must be by menstruation.
This is the detailed ruling chosen in al-Nahr and al-Mujtabā.

Source Text

وأكثر المشايخ قدروه بستين سنة ، ومشايخ بُخارا وخَوَارَزْم بخمس وخمسين سنة فما رأت بعدها لا يكون حيضاً في ظاهر المذهب، والمختار أنَّها إن رأت دماً قوياً كالأسود والأحمر القاني كان حيضاً ، ويبطل الاعتداد بالأشهر قبل التمام وبعده لا . قلت : الأصحية راجعة إلى نفس التوقيت لا إلى إطلاق الحيض، فلا تنافي، وللناظرين هاهنا كلمات بينا ما لها وما عليها في «السعاية». [1] قوله : وأكثر المشايخ ... الخ ؛ قال العَيْني في «البناية»: «اختلف في زمان الإياس : فقيل : ستون، وعن محمد الله» في «المولدات»: ستون، وفي «الروميات»: خمس وخمسون ، وقيل : يعتبر أقرانها من قرابتها ، وقيل : يعتبر تركيبها ؛ لاختلاف الطبائع باختلاف البلدان ، وقيل : خمس وخمسون، والفتوى في زماننا عليه». [٢]قوله : ويبطل ؛ يعني لو طلقت الآيسة فاعتدت بالأشهر بناءً على أنّ عدة الآيسة ثلاثة شهور ثم عاد دمها قوياً، فإن كان ذلك في أثناء تلك الأشهر يحكم ببطلان تلك العدة، ويجب عليها استئناف العدة بثلاثة حيض ؛ لتبين كونها ذات حيض، وإن كان ذلك بعد تمام الأشهر الثلاثة لا يحكم ببطلانها، حتى لو نكحت زوجاً آخر بعد ثلاث أشهر لا يفسد ذلك النكاح. نعم يجب عليها العدة في المستقبل بالحيض، وهذا التفصيل هو الذي اختاره في «النهر» وقال: «هو أعدلُ الروايات»، وفي المجتبى»: «إنّه الصحيحُ المختار»
And most of the mashāyikh estimated it as sixty years, and the mashāyikh of Bukhārā and Khawārizm as fifty-five years. So what she sees after it is not menstruation in the apparent madhhab, and the chosen view is that if she sees strong blood like black or deep red, it is menstruation, and the 'iddah by months is invalidated before completion, but not after. I say: the soundness pertains to the timing itself, not to the application of menstruation, so there is no contradiction. And for the commentators here there are words, we have explained what supports and what opposes them in 'al-Sa'āyah'. [1] His statement: 'And most of the mashāyikh...' etc.; al-'Aynī said in 'al-Bināyah': 'There is disagreement concerning the time of menopause: it was said sixty, and from Muhammad (Allah?) in 'al-Mawlidāt': sixty, and in 'al-Rūmiyyāt': fifty-five, and it was said that one considers her peers from her relatives, and it was said that one considers her constitution due to difference of natures with difference of lands, and it was said fifty-five, and the fatwa in our time is upon it.' [2] His statement: 'and it is invalidated'; meaning if a menopausal woman is divorced and performs 'iddah by months based on that the 'iddah of a menopausal woman is three months, then her blood returns strongly, if that is during those months, it is ruled that that 'iddah is invalidated, and she must start the 'iddah anew with three menstruations because it becomes evident that she is a menstruating woman; and if that is after the completion of the three months, it is not ruled invalid, even if she marries another husband after three months, that marriage is not invalidated. Yes, she must perform 'iddah in the future by menstruation. And this detail is what was chosen in 'al-Nahr' and he said: 'It is the most balanced of the narrations', and in 'al-Mujtabā': 'It is the correct and chosen one.'
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'āyah is a commentary on al-Wiqāyah dealing with the age of menopause (īyās) and its effect on 'iddah. The passage opens by stating a dispute among Hanafi scholars regarding the age of menopause. Most mashāyikh set it at sixty years, while the mashāyikh of Bukhārā and Khawārizm set it at fifty-five. According to the apparent madhhab (ẓāhir al-madhhab), any blood seen after the age of īyās is not considered menstruation. However, the chosen view (al-mukhtār) is that if a woman sees strong blood — black or deep red — it is menstruation. This is because strong blood indicates vitality and fertility, so she is not truly menopausal. The commentary then explains a critical ruling: If a menopausal woman (who thought she was īyās) divorces and begins her 'iddah by months (three months, since her blood was assumed to be istiḥāḍah), and then during those months she sees strong blood, her 'iddah by months is invalidated. She must instead observe 'iddah by three full menstrual cycles (qurūʾ). However, if the strong blood appears after the three months have ended, the 'iddah by months is valid, and any subsequent marriage is not affected. Nevertheless, she must observe 'iddah by menstruation in the future. The commentary further cites al-ʿAynī from al-Bināyah, detailing the various opinions on the exact age of īyās: sixty, fifty-five, or determination by peers or constitution. The fatwa in the author's time is on fifty-five. This detail is supported by al-Nahr and al-Mujtabā as the soundest and chosen position. Note that the dispute is intra-Hanafi; all agree that the ruling on blood after īyās depends on its strength, not just its appearance.

Key Terms
الإياس (al-īyās): The age beyond which a woman's blood is normally not considered menstrual; disputed between 55 and 60 years in the Hanafi school.
الاعتداد بالأشهر (al-iʿtidād bil-ashhur): The 'iddah (waiting period) observed by three months instead of three menstrual cycles, applicable to post-menopausal women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the 'iddah by months of a menopausal woman if she sees strong blood during the three-month period?
A) The 'iddah by months remains valid, and she completes it.
B) The 'iddah by months is invalidated, and she must start a new 'iddah of three menstrual cycles.
C) She continues with months but adds extra months.
D) She must wait until the blood stops, then continue.

Key Takeaway
The determination of menstruation in older women depends on the strength of blood, not solely on age; the chosen Hanafi view sets menopause at 55, but strong blood overrides that presumption.

Menstruation Duration: Minimum, Maximum, and the Hanafi Proof
Ruling on minimum/maximum menstruation with proofs and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi minimum and maximum for menstruation, compare the disputes with Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i, and identify the proof (dalil) used.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school sets menstruation at 3-10 days based on a prophetic hadith, rejecting alternate opinions.

This lesson addresses the fundamental ruling on the duration of menstruation (hayd). The Hanafi school establishes a clear minimum and maximum based on a specific hadith, and contrasts it with other scholarly opinions. Understanding this ruling is crucial for distinguishing hayd from istihadah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the minimum (3 days and nights) and maximum (10 days) as per the relied-upon Hanafi view.
This is based on the hadith cited in the passage.
2
Identify the intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab ikhtilaf
Note that Abu Yusuf (within Hanafi) sets minimum at 2 days, and al-Shafi'i sets minimum at 1 day/night and maximum at 15 days.
The source also mentions other opinions but does not detail them.
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The hadith quoted: 'The minimum of menstruation for a virgin and a non-virgin is three days and their nights, and its maximum is ten days.' This hadith is narrated by multiple chains.
The Hanafi school relies on this explicit textual evidence.
4
Understand the Hanafi reliance on this hadith
The hadith is zanni al-thubut (transmissionally probable) but qati al-dalalah (textually definitive), so it is binding. It is not overridden by istihsan.
Contrast with Shafi'i who uses other hadiths and reasoning.
5
Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
A woman bleeding for 2 days is in istihadah according to Hanafi (except Abu Yusuf), but would be in menstruation according to Shafi'i.
This affects rulings on prayer, fasting, and marital relations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأقله ثلاثة أيام ولياليها ، وأكثره عشرة ، وعند أبي يوسف له أقله يومان ، وأكثر من اليوم الثالث ، وعند الشَّافِعِي له أقله يوم وليلة، وأكثره خمسة عشر ، ونحن نتمسك بقوله : أَقَلُّ الحَيْضِ لِلجَارِيَةِ البِكْرِ وَالتَّيْبِ ثَلاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ وَلَيَالِيهَا ، وَأَكْثَرُهُ عَشْرَةُ أَيَّامٍ . واختار في «الهداية» بطلان العدة بالأشهر بعود الدم مطلقاً، وفي المسألة أقوال أخر مبسوم سوطة في «البحر». قوله : وإن رأت ; الآيسة بعد المدة المذكورة صُفرة بالضم بالفارسية : زردي ، أو خُضرة بالضم بالفارسية : سبنري، أو تُرَبيّة - بضم التاء المثناة الفوقية، وفتح الراء المهملة وكسر الباء الموحدة، وتشديد الياء المثناة التحتية : اللون الذي يشبه التراب ، فهي استحاضة، وهذا إذا لم تكن عادته كذلك، فإن كانت عادتها قبل الإياس الصفرة أو الخضرة أو التربية يكون ذلك حيضاً. كذا في «فتح القدير». قوله : بقوله... الخ؛ هذا الحديث أخرجه الطبراني من حديث أبي أمامة، والدارقطني من حديث واثلة ، وابن عدي من حديث معاذ ، وابن الجوزي من حديث أبي سعيد الخدري له ، وابن عدي من حديث أنس له وغيرهم
And its minimum is three days and their nights, and its maximum is ten. And according to Abū Yūsuf, its minimum is two days and more than the third day, and according to al-Shāfiʿī, its minimum is a day and a night, and its maximum is fifteen. And we adhere to his statement: 'The minimum of menstruation for a virgin and a non-virgin is three days and their nights, and its maximum is ten days.' And he chose in 'al-Hidāyah' the invalidation of 'iddah by months with the return of blood absolutely, and there are other opinions in the matter detailed in 'al-Baḥr'. His statement: 'And if she sees' — meaning the menopausal woman after the mentioned duration — yellow (in Persian: zardī), or green (in Persian: sabzī), or earthy — with ḍammah on the tā', fatḥah on the rā', kasrah on the bā', and tashdīd on the yā': the color resembling earth — then it is istiḥāḍah. This is if that is not her habit; if her habit before menopause was yellow or green or earthy, then that is menstruation. As in 'Fatḥ al-Qadīr'. His statement: 'by his statement... etc.'; this ḥadīth was narrated by al-Ṭabarānī from Abū Umāmah, al-Dāraquṭnī from Wāthilah, Ibn ʿAdī from Muʿādh, Ibn al-Jawzī from Abū Saʿīd al-Khudrī, Ibn ʿAdī from Anas, and others.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'āyah addresses foundational rulings on menstruation (ḥayḍ) and non-menstrual bleeding (istiḥāḍah). It begins by stating the minimum duration of menstruation: three complete days and nights, and the maximum: ten days. This is the established Hanafi position. The text then presents the opinions of Abū Yūsuf (minimum two days) and al-Shāfiʿī (minimum one day and night, maximum fifteen) to highlight the inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi school relies on a ḥadīth of the Prophet (ṣallallāhu ʿalayhi wa sallam): 'The minimum of menstruation for a virgin and a non-virgin is three days and their nights, and its maximum is ten days.' This ḥadīth is cited as the proof (dalīl) for the Hanafi position. The commentary then mentions that al-Hidāyah chooses the absolute invalidation of 'iddah by months if blood returns, but does not elaborate further. Next, the definition of istiḥāḍah is given: if a woman (especially a menopausal woman) sees yellow, green, or earthy discharge after the age of īyās, it is istiḥāḍah, not menstruation. However, an important exception is noted: if such discharge was her habitual menstrual flow before menopause, then it is considered menstruation. This is based on the principle that habitual color and consistency are taken into account. The ḥadīth's chain of narration is also provided, indicating its authenticity according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
الحيض (al-ḥayḍ): Menstrual blood; its minimum duration is three full days and nights, maximum ten days.
الاستحاضة (al-istiḥāḍah): Non-menstrual bleeding; its rules differ from hayd.
أقل الحيض (aqall al-ḥayḍ): The minimum duration of menstruation according to Hanafi: 3 days and nights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), what is the minimum duration of menstruation?
A) One day and one night
B) Two days
C) Three days and their nights
D) Five days

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi minimum of 3 days for menstruation is firmly based on a prophetic hadith, and any shorter bleeding is considered istihadah.
